2:21:1072:0:14:72:289:700:12:Times:12:Times:!:Education Research and Administrative Data
2:22:1114:14:14:72:369:686:12:Times:12:Times:!:David N. Figlio, Krzysztof Karbownik, and Kjell G. Salvanes
2:23:1173:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:!:NBER Working Paper No. 21592

2:26:1226:28:28:306:339:616:12:Times:12:Times:!:ABSTRACT
2:27:1234:28:14:72:540:588:12:Times:12:Times:!:Thanks to extraordinary and exponential improvements in data storage and computing capacities, it
2:28:1331:14:14:72:540:574:12:Times:12:Times:!:is now possible to collect, manage, and analyze data in magnitudes and in manners that would have
2:29:1428:14:14:72:540:560:12:Times:12:Times:!:been inconceivable just a short time ago. As the world has developed this remarkable capacity to store
2:30:1530:14:14:72:540:546:12:Times:12:Times:!:and analyze data, so have the world’s governments developed large-scale, comprehensive data files
2:31:1627:14:14:72:540:532:12:Times:12:Times:!:on tax programs, workforce information, benefit programs, health, and education. While these data
2:32:1724:14:14:72:540:518:12:Times:12:Times:!:are collected for purely administrative purposes, they represent remarkable new opportunities for expanding
2:33:1831:14:14:72:540:504:12:Times:12:Times:!:our knowledge. This chapter describes some of the benefits and challenges associated with the use
2:34:1928:14:14:72:540:490:12:Times:12:Times:!:of administrative data in education research. We also offer specific case studies of data that have been
2:35:2032:14:14:72:540:476:12:Times:12:Times:!:developed in both the Nordic countries and the United States, and offer an (incomplete) inventory
2:36:2129:14:42:72:540:462:12:Times:12:Times:!:of data sets used by social scientists to study education questions on every inhabited continent on earth.
2:37:2235:42:14:72:148:420:12:Times:12:Times:!:David N. Figlio
2:38:2250:14:14:72:209:406:12:Times:12:Times:!:Institute for Policy Research
2:39:2279:14:14:72:191:392:12:Times:12:Times:!:Northwestern University
2:40:2302:14:14:72:170:378:12:Times:12:Times:!:2040 Sheridan Road
2:41:2320:14:14:72:167:364:12:Times:12:Times:!:Evanston, IL 60208
2:42:2338:14:14:72:124:350:12:Times:12:Times:!:and NBER
2:43:2346:14:28:72:192:336:12:Times:12:Times:!:figlio@northwestern.edu
2:44:2369:28:14:72:176:308:12:Times:12:Times:!:Krzysztof Karbownik

2:46:2417:14:14:72:191:280:12:Times:12:Times:!:Northwestern University
2:47:2440:14:14:72:170:266:12:Times:12:Times:!:2040 Sheridan Road

2:55:2608:14:14:306:345:364:12:Times:12:Times:!:Norway
2:56:2614:14:14:306:400:350:12:Times:12:Times:!:and IZA and CEPR

3:58:2651:0:20:189:425:708:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Education Research and Administrative Data 
3:59:2693:20:21:90:168:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:C:I. Introduction 
3:60:2708:21:20:126:525:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A: Thanks  to  extraordinary  and  exponential  improvements  in  data  storage  and 
3:61:2790:20:21:90:525:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:computing  capacities,  it  is  now  possible  to  collect,  manage,  and  analyze  data  in 
3:62:2883:21:21:90:525:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:magnitudes  and  in  manners  that  would  have  been  inconceivable  just  a  short  time  ago. 
3:63:2980:21:21:90:524:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:From 1986 to 2007, the world’s capacity to store data increased from 539 MB per capita 
3:64:3066:21:20:90:525:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:to  44,716  MB  per  capita,  with  81  percent  of  that  growth  occurring  over  the  last  seven 
3:65:3167:20:21:90:525:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:years  of  that  time  period  (Hilbert  and  Lopez,  2011).  Over  the  same  time  period, 
3:66:3260:21:21:90:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:computing  speed  increased  at  an  even  faster  pace – from  0.09  million  instructions  per 
3:67:3356:21:20:90:524:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:second  on  general-purpose  computers  in  1986  to  239  million  instructions  per  second  in 
3:68:3454:20:21:90:525:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:2000  to  28,620  million  instructions  per  second  in  2007  (Hilbert  and  Lopez,  2011).  And 
3:69:3553:21:21:90:524:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:while we do not have comparable statistics for the past seven years, computing speed and 
3:70:3642:21:21:90:323:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:capacity growth has surely continued unabated.  
3:71:3689:21:20:126:525:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A: As the world has developed this remarkable capacity to store and analyze data, so 
3:72:3771:20:21:90:524:419:12:g_d0_f3:12:Times New Roman:B:have the world’s governments developed large-scale,  comprehensive  data  files  on  tax 
3:73:3860:21:21:90:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:programs,  workforce  information,  benefit  programs,  health,  and  education.  Today,  in 
3:74:3953:21:20:90:525:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:many countries around the world, governments collect, maintain, and store an archive of 
3:75:4041:20:21:90:524:357:12:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f3:B:information regarding a vast range of behaviors and outcomes over an individual’s entire 
3:76:4130:21:21:90:524:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:lifetime  (Card  et  al,  2010).  Governments have  established  statistical  offices  to  maintain 
3:77:4230:21:20:90:525:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and use  these  data  to  produce official  statistics  about  their  populations. In  the  education 
3:78:4331:20:21:90:524:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:sector,  governments  have  invested  large sums  of  funds  to  develop  longitudinal  data 
3:79:4424:21:21:90:525:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:systems.  For  example,  in  the  United  States,  the  federal  Department  of  Education  has 
3:80:4520:21:21:90:525:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:invested  over  $750  million  to  help  states  build,  populate,  and  maintain  these  data 
3:81:4615:21:20:90:524:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:systems. Much  of  this  innovation  in  the  United States  came  about  as  part  of  school 
3:82:4709:20:21:90:525:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:accountability  systems,  and  accountability  systems  still  provide  the  backbone  for  the 
3:83:4805:21:21:90:294:191:12:g_d0_f3:12:Times New Roman:B:country’s most frequently used databases. 
3:84:4846:21:20:126:525:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:At   the   same   time,   because   administrative data   sets   are   established   for 
3:85:4935:20:21:90:525:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:administrative  purposes,  they  are  not  designed  in  a  manner  that  makes  them  readily 
3:86:5030:21:21:90:524:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:available  for  scholarly  activity. In  many  locations,  the data  sets  are  administered  by 
3:87:5127:21:21:90:525:108:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:officials who also implement the policies for which these data were collected, and those 
3:88:5214:21:0:90:524:87:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:who  control  access  to  the  data  may  not  be  interested  in  evaluation  of  the  policies  they 
4:89:5318:0:21:90:525:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:oversee.  Moreover,  the  structure  of  administrative  data – with  a  set  of  records  for  each 
4:90:5418:21:21:90:525:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:administrative  event,  be  it  a  point  in  time  record  about  school  attendance  or  workforce 
4:91:5519:21:20:90:525:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:participation, a test score, a disciplinary infraction, a residential move, or a class taken – 
4:92:5613:20:21:90:525:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:offers both complications and new opportunities of statistical analysis along a vast range 
4:93:5704:21:21:90:193:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of substantive areas.  
4:94:5726:21:21:126:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:While  these  data  are  collected  for  purely administrative  purposes,  they  represent 
4:95:5816:21:20:90:524:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:remarkable new opportunities for expanding our knowledge and, through the conduct of 
4:96:5901:20:21:90:525:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:analyses  with  more  comprehensive  data  and  better  sources  of  exogenous  variation  than 
4:97:5997:21:21:90:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:could  typically  be  used  in  times  past, challenging conventional  wisdom  in  many  areas 
4:98:6090:21:20:90:525:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:based on previous research utilizing other sources like surveys. Administrative data also 
4:99:6179:20:21:90:525:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:facilitate  study  of  research  questions  that  have  heretofore  not  been  possible  to  study 
4:100:6278:21:21:90:524:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:credibly at all. Researchers who are able to access these data, especially those able to link 
4:101:6372:21:21:90:525:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:data  across  administrative  domains,  have  the  ability  to  make  extraordinary  scientific 
4:102:6468:21:20:90:525:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:advances by  exploiting  the  population-wide  data  sets  combined  with  the increased 
4:103:6556:20:21:90:525:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:opportunity for  identification  of  causal  effects  through  exogenous  variation  by, for 
4:104:6648:21:21:90:524:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:instance, policy  changes,  natural  disasters,  and  other  shocks  that  affect  some  groups  of 
4:105:6747:21:20:90:525:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:people  but  not  others. In  addition  to  natural  experiments,  these  data  can  facilitate  the 
4:106:6848:20:21:90:525:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:conduct  of  field  experiments,  where  the  subjects  of  short-term  experiments  can  be 
4:107:6941:21:21:90:525:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:followed  administratively  for  a  longer  period  of  time  in  manners  that  would  have  been 
4:108:7040:21:20:90:524:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:impossible or prohibitively expensive to do absent large-scale administratively-collected 
4:109:7130:20:21:90:525:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:data. The  new  insights  from  these  studies  have extraordinary potential  to inform 
4:110:7217:21:21:90:525:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:education  policy  and  practice,  and  we  document  some  cases  where  new  policies have 
4:111:7310:21:21:90:525:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:been based upon  insights  from  these  studies. Indeed,  the  massive  growth  in  the  quality 
4:112:7407:21:20:90:525:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and  diversity  of  economic  research  on  educational  topics  is  certainly  related  to  the 
4:113:7504:20:21:90:333:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:increased availability of good administrative data. 
4:114:7555:21:21:126:524:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:This chapter describes some of the benefits and challenges associated with the use 
4:115:7638:21:20:90:525:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of  administrative  data  in  education  research. We  also  offer  specific  case  studies  of  data 
4:116:7739:20:21:90:525:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:that have been developed in both the Nordic countries and the United States, and offer an 
4:117:7829:21:21:90:525:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:(incomplete)  inventory  of  data  sets  used  by  economists  to  study  education  questions  on 
4:118:7928:21:21:90:259:108:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:every inhabited continent on earth. 
4:119:7963:21:0:126:129:87:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:!: 
5:120:7964:21:20:90:431:708:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:C:II. The benefits of using administrative data in education research 
5:121:8031:20:21:126:525:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A: Administrative  data  sets  are  not  a  panacea.  They  are  limited  to  certain  locations, 
5:122:8126:21:20:90:524:667:12:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f3:B:which  can decrease generalizability. It’s hard to know whether a research study from 
5:123:8211:20:21:90:525:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Colombia or North Carolina or Norway or Romania will translate into different contexts. 
5:124:8299:21:21:90:525:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Administrative  data  sets  often  measure  variables  in  a  manner  that  is  conducive  to 
5:125:8393:21:21:90:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:administration of programs, say, but are not necessarily ideal for research purposes. And 
5:126:8483:21:20:90:524:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:administrative  data  sets  are  not  necessarily  structured  in  a  manner  that  ensures  data 
5:127:8581:20:21:90:385:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:quality similar to the one in purpose-built research data sets.  
5:128:8645:21:21:126:524:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:That   said,   while   traditional   purpose-built data   sets   have   many   strengths, 
5:129:8735:21:20:90:524:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:administrative data  sets  offer  a  number  of  clear  advantages  for  empirical  research  in 
5:130:8832:20:21:90:524:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:education.  One  clear  advantage  involves  the  ability  to  study  population-level  data.  This 
5:131:8932:21:21:90:525:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:ability  offers  a  number  of  remarkable  new  possibilities.  Perhaps  the  most  obvious 
5:132:9025:21:21:90:524:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:involves  statistical  power – in  contrast  to data  sets  with  hundreds  or  thousands  of 
5:133:9118:21:20:90:524:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:observations, administrative data sets with many times that number of observations mean 
5:134:9206:20:21:90:525:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:that  it  is  often  (depending  on  research  design)  possible  to  detect  modest  but  meaningful 
5:135:9308:21:21:90:524:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:relationships  with  much  greater  precision  than  was  previously  possible.  But  there  are  at 
5:136:9409:21:20:90:525:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:least  two  other  distinct  advantages  of  administrative  data  that  are  afforded  by  the  large 
5:137:9512:20:21:90:525:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:magnitudes  of  observations.  One  involves  the  ability  to  detect  rare  events  that  might  be 
5:138:9614:21:21:90:525:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:useful  for  identification: In  administrative data  sets,  it  is  often  possible  to  make  twin 
5:139:9715:21:20:90:524:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:comparisons  or  study  children  from  three-child  families;  to  investigate  the  effects  of 
5:140:9813:20:21:90:525:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:extremely rare climatic or seismic events; or to study specific economic events like plant 
5:141:9903:21:21:90:525:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:closures (Card et al, 2010; Roed and Raaum, 2003). In traditional purpose-built data sets, 
5:142:9994:21:21:90:525:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:it  is  rare  to  have  sufficient  numbers  of  observations  to  be  able  to  carry  out  analyses  of 
5:143:10100:21:20:90:525:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:these  types.  Another  major  advantage  of  having  large-scale  administrative  data  is  the 
5:144:10197:20:21:90:525:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:ability  to  study  heterogeneous  effects  of  educational  policies  and  practice:  With  very 
5:145:10295:21:21:90:525:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:large numbers of observations, it becomes possible to see whether the effects are similar 
5:146:10385:21:20:90:525:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:across wildly different  groups of individuals, and if they differ, how they  differ, and for 
5:147:10479:20:21:90:129:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:whom.  
5:148:10485:21:21:126:525:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Allowing   for   new   identification   strategies   and   for   the   ability   to   see   how 
5:149:10581:21:21:90:524:108:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:generalizable results are  across  groups are two major advantages of the population-level 
5:150:10672:21:0:90:524:87:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:nature of administrative data, but they are not the only benefits. Because data coverage is 
6:151:10765:0:21:90:525:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:universal,  it  becomes  feasible  that  one  can  link  administrative  data  from  one  domain 
6:152:10862:21:21:90:524:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:(e.g.,  education)  to  data  from  another  domain  (e.g.,  workforce  or  health). While  it  is 
6:153:10961:21:20:90:524:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:certainly  possible  to  compare  across  domains  in non-administrative  settings,  doing  so  is 
6:154:11059:20:21:90:525:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:considerably more difficult because people would have to be purposefully longitudinally 
6:155:11147:21:21:90:525:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:followed,  and  because  a  cross-section  of  educational  data,  say,  and  a  cross-section  of 
6:156:11246:21:21:90:524:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:health   data   may   only   include   some   of   the   same   individuals   by   happenstance. 
6:157:11343:21:20:90:524:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Administrative data, by  virtue of their population-level nature and the  frequency of data 
6:158:11435:20:21:90:525:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:observation, allow the researcher to follow individuals or entities over time, so that there 
6:159:11528:21:21:90:242:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:is a panel structure to the data.  
6:160:11561:21:20:126:524:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Administrative data sets also provide novel types of variables typically not found 
6:161:11644:20:21:90:524:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:in  non-administrative  data  (Einav  and  Levin,  2013).  They  can  offer  new  opportunities, 
6:162:11741:21:21:90:525:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:for  instance,  to  look  at  measures  of  delinquency,  of  changing  geographical  location,  of 
6:163:11841:21:21:90:524:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:social  networks,  and  of  health  instances  that  are  nearly  impossible  to  study  in  any  other 
6:164:11945:21:20:90:525:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:manner. The  real-time  nature  of  administrative  data  also  provides new  opportunities  to 
6:165:12040:20:21:90:525:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:study the effects of educational policies and practices that are very recent; and offers the 
6:166:12132:21:21:90:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:chance  for  researchers  to  make  their  scholarship  much  more  relevant  to  the  specific 
6:167:12228:21:20:90:525:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:policy decisions that policymakers must make right away than are studies that make use 
6:168:12315:20:21:90:524:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of retrospective information (Einav and Levin, 2013). And of course, natural experiments 
6:169:12403:21:21:90:525:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:need  not  be  rare  events  to  be  better-studied  using  administrative data  sets:  Because 
6:170:12499:21:20:90:525:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:natural  experiments  are  unannounced,  and  often  occur  via  chance  or  quirks,  it  is  very 
6:171:12598:20:21:90:524:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:difficult  to  set  up  a  prospective  study  that  will  permit  the  evaluation  of  a  natural 
6:172:12697:21:21:90:525:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:experiment;  with  administrative  data  that  cover  a  population  and  that  are  recorded 
6:173:12791:21:21:90:525:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:regularly, it is much more feasible to ex post identify and study these natural experiments 
6:174:12883:21:20:90:216:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:(Roed and Raaum, 2003). 
6:175:12906:20:21:126:525:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:The  preceding  description  of  advantages  of  administrative  data  makes  clear  the 
6:176:12995:21:21:90:525:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:benefits  of  these  data  for  identifying  causal  effects.  But  these  data  are  also  highly 
6:177:13094:21:20:90:524:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:beneficial  for  the  identification  of  structural  parameters  of  human  behavior for  multiple 
6:178:13194:20:21:90:525:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:reasons.  First  of  all, the  population-level  nature  of  administrative  data  means  that  these 
6:179:13296:21:21:90:525:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:data are representative of a given population. In addition, the administrative data, through 
6:180:13389:21:21:90:525:108:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the variety of records across a set of domains, both simultaneously and over-time, allows 
6:181:13479:21:0:90:525:87:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the  structural  analyst  with  the  opportunity  to  simultaneously  model  a  set  of  complex 
7:182:13577:0:21:90:522:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:relationships  that  would  almost  surely  not  be  possible  to  uncover  using  retrospectively-
7:183:13676:21:21:90:524:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:collected data (Roed and Raaum, 2003). The lack of a specific structure of administrative 
7:184:13766:21:20:90:525:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:data can  also facilitate reduced-form analyses, because data that are recorded as a series 
7:185:13858:20:21:90:525:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of  observations  but  without  a  distinct  structure  can  be  rearranged  to  build  rectangular 
7:186:13958:21:21:90:524:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:panel  data  sets  that  have  precisely  the  properties  that  are more ideal  for  the  specific 
7:187:14057:21:21:90:322:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:empirical task at hand (Eivan and Levin, 2013). 
7:188:14104:21:20:126:525:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Another  benefit  of  administrative  data  is  that  data  quality  is  likely  to  be  simply 
7:189:14200:20:21:90:524:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:better than retrospective data collection. Rather than ask people whether they participated 
7:190:14292:21:21:90:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:in a  given program twenty  years ago, scholars who make use of administrative data can 
7:191:14380:21:20:90:524:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:observe  directly  whether  the  individuals  participated – according  to  the  authorities  who 
7:192:14477:20:21:90:525:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:paid  for  the  participation  and  therefore  had  a  strong  interest  in  correctly  recording  the 
7:193:14580:21:21:90:525:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:occurrence!  Also  because  of  the  mandatory  nature  of  participation  in  the  activities  that 
7:194:14681:21:21:90:525:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:generate  administrative  data,  these  data  are  much  less  likely  to  suffer  from  attrition 
7:195:14780:21:20:90:525:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:problems  or  non-response  problems  than  are  data  collected  through  voluntary  means 
7:196:14872:20:21:90:522:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:(Card  et  al.,  2010).  Likewise,  administrative  data  are  likely  to  be  less  subject  to  over-
7:197:14975:21:21:90:310:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:reporting or under-reporting of key variables. 
7:198:15021:21:20:126:525:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Administrative  data  also  facilitate  the  study  of  intergenerational  issues.  It  is 
7:199:15112:20:21:90:525:357:12:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f3:B:possible,  at  least  in  some contexts, to match children’s administrative records to that of 
7:200:15206:21:21:90:525:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:their parents, and even grandparents. While it is certainly possible to purposefully follow 
7:201:15298:21:20:90:525:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:families  longitudinally,  the  risk  of  attrition  is  surely  greater  when  attempting  to  move 
7:202:15399:20:21:90:525:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:from  one generation to  the  next  than  if  it  is  possible  to  directly  match  individuals  using 
7:203:15502:21:21:90:524:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:administrative means (Roed and Raaum, 2003). And, in the case of questions that require 
7:204:15590:21:21:90:525:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:a  long  amount  of  time  to  study  in  real  time  (e.g.,  intergenerational  isssues), the  time 
7:205:15690:21:20:90:525:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:horizon   over   which   intergenerational   questions   may   be   studied   can   be   shrunk 
7:206:15786:20:21:90:276:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:considerably with administrative data. 
7:207:15823:21:21:126:525:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Using administrative data has major practical value as well. Importantly, different 
7:208:15906:21:20:90:525:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:countries have extremely different policy environments. While it is possible that in some 
7:209:15996:20:21:90:525:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:circumstances, a study conducted in Denmark would be just as relevant to Chile as would 
7:210:16084:21:21:90:524:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:be a study conducted in Chile, or vice versa, there are many cases – because of different 
7:211:16173:21:21:90:524:108:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:institutions and different populations – where it makes the most sense to study a specific 
7:212:16263:21:0:90:525:87:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:question in the location where the policy environment is what the researcher most wishes 
8:213:16353:0:21:90:525:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:to  study.  And,  of  course,  this  demonstrates  the  real  benefit  of  comparative  work  across 
8:214:16454:21:21:90:524:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:jurisdictions:  If  a  result  is  similar  across  very  different  populations  or  very  different 
8:215:16556:21:20:90:525:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:policy  environments,  this  lends  additional  credence  to  the  idea  that  the  result  is  general. 
8:216:16661:20:21:90:525:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Likewise,   we   can   learn   a   lot   from   studying   how   different are the   outcomes   in 
8:217:16758:21:21:90:525:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:jurisdictions  where  the  policy  environment  is  very  different  from  one  another.  In  sum, 
8:218:16857:21:21:90:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:some research is transferrable and we can learn a lot from work done in other countries, 
8:219:16946:21:20:90:525:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:but  other  research  is  best  conducted  locally,  suggesting  a  benefit  to  many  countries 
8:220:17043:20:21:90:524:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:developing,  maintaining, and  sharing  with  researchers  their  administrative  data  (Card  et 
8:221:17140:21:21:90:144:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:al., 2010).  
8:222:17152:21:20:126:525:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:In  summary,  administrative  data  are  more  comprehensive  than  are  purpose-built 
8:223:17239:20:21:90:525:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:survey  data,  and  can  be  collected  with  frequently  far  more  accurate  information. 
8:224:17331:21:21:90:524:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Furthermore, the costs of conducting research with administrative data are much lower as 
8:225:17420:21:21:90:525:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:well,  at  least  once  the  data  systems  are  developed.  Once  data  structures  are  established, 
8:226:17523:21:20:90:525:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:linking  and  extracting  more  records  from  administrative  data  cost  only  the  time  of  the 
8:227:17623:20:21:90:525:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:programmer, and the marginal cost of adding additional individuals or periods of data to 
8:228:17712:21:21:90:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the analytical sample is extremely small, suggesting remarkably large economies of scale 
8:229:17801:21:20:90:525:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:associated  with administrative data (Roed and Raaum, 2003). While there are obviously 
8:230:17888:20:21:90:524:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:many  important  roles  for  purpose-built  survey  data – not  least  the  fact  that  only  with 
8:231:17986:21:21:90:524:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:purpose-built data it is possible to study precisely the questions that one wishes to study 
8:232:18078:21:20:90:524:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:in exactly the  manner  in  which  one  wishes  to  study  them – it  is  also  evident  that 
8:233:18171:20:21:90:525:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:administrative  data  offer  numerous  new  opportunities  to  conduct  research  on  questions 
8:234:18267:21:21:90:524:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:that   were   previously   impossible   to   study,   or   at   least   to   study so well.   Indeed, 
8:235:18369:21:21:90:525:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:administrative  data and  survey  data,  while  sometimes  substitutes,  can  frequently  be 
8:236:18461:21:20:90:525:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:considered complements, as when administrative data can reduce the set of questions that 
8:237:18550:20:21:90:525:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:need  to  be  answered  via  surveys,  or  when  administrative  data  can  be  used  to  serve  as  a 
8:238:18653:21:21:90:524:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:check  on  the  reliability  of  retrospective  information  collected  via  surveys  (Roed  and 
8:239:18750:21:20:90:525:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Raaum,  2003).  Administrative  data  can  also  be  thought  of  as  complementary  to  the 
8:240:18843:20:21:90:525:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:conduct  of  field  experiments,  as  the  costs  of  tracking  and  following  up  with  field 
8:241:18939:21:21:90:525:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:experiment  participants  are  much  lower,  and  the  data  frequently  much  better,  when  the 
8:242:19037:21:21:90:524:108:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:field  experiments  can  be  linked  with  data  collected by governments  for  administrative 
8:243:19131:21:0:90:525:87:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:purposes (Card et al., 2010). For all of these purposes, having a high degree of access to 
9:244:19223:0:21:90:524:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:administrative data  makes  a  wide  range  of  empirical  studies  in  education  more  feasible 
9:245:19320:21:21:90:193:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and more believable. 
9:246:19340:21:14:90:93:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:!: 
9:247:19340:35:13:90:176:653:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:C:III. Case studies 
9:248:19357:13:21:126:129:640:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:!: 
9:249:19357:34:21:126:524:619:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:The  Nordic  countries,  notably  Denmark, Sweden,  Norway, Finland  and  to  some 
9:250:19439:21:20:90:522:598:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:extent  Iceland, established  administrative  registers  in  the  mid-1960s.  When  population-
9:251:19533:20:21:90:524:578:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:wide  social  security  systems  were established,  there  was  a  need  for  a  unique  personal 
9:252:19630:21:21:90:525:557:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:identifier  in  order  to  follow people across  jobs  and  other  labor  market  states and collect 
9:253:19729:21:21:90:525:536:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:information  on  earned  pension  points.  These population-wide  identifiers  were  then 
9:254:19817:21:20:90:524:515:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:adopted for all administrative registers from birth registers to cause of death registers, and 
9:255:19911:20:21:90:525:495:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:included in  registers  covering education and labor  market  participation, as  well  as for 
9:256:20003:21:21:90:524:474:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:linking  members  of  families  together.  The  core  of  these  registers  is  thus  the  universal 
9:257:20104:21:20:90:524:453:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:system for identification numbers covering everybody from date of birth (or immigration) 
9:258:20193:20:21:90:525:433:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and identical across all administrative units. The identification number system was based 
9:259:20283:21:21:90:525:412:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:on the 1960 census and for some of the countries also local (municipality level) registries 
9:260:20375:21:21:90:525:391:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of populations. This also implies then that people born several decades prior to 1960 are 
9:261:20464:21:20:90:524:370:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:covered. And for instance for Norway, a job has been done more recently to uncover time 
9:262:20552:20:21:90:477:350:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and place of birth, and for some registers and cohorts also parental background.  
9:263:20633:21:21:126:525:329:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:The  Nordic  countries  have  established  mechanisms  to  share  these  data  with 
9:264:20717:21:20:90:524:308:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:members  of  the  research  community  for  specific  research  projects,  and  several  research 
9:265:20815:20:21:90:524:288:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:groups  in  each  country  have  now  access  to portions  of  the  register data  linking  some  of 
9:266:20915:21:21:90:524:267:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:these data sets depending on the focus of research.1 In the case of each research project, 
9:267:21005:21:20:90:525:246:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:both  the  administrative  units  who  administer  the  data  as  well as  the  national Data 
9:268:21098:20:21:90:525:226:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Inspection  Authority must consent  to  the  use  and  matching  of  registers  based  on  a 
9:269:21190:21:21:90:524:205:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:detailed  application  procedure. Since  the  registers  contain  sensitive  and  very  private 
9:270:21286:21:21:90:525:184:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:information,  the  national  statistical  offices  link  the  registers for  research  purposes  and 
9:271:21387:21:20:90:524:163:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:provide   identification numbers   for   researchers   that   are   different   from   the   actual 
9:272:21487:20:32:90:279:143:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:administrative identification numbers.  
9:273:21526:32:11:234:237:111:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:!:                                                        
9:274:21581:43:15:90:510:100:8:g_d0_f4:10:Times New Roman:D:1 This overview focus on registers used for research with a focus on education in wide sense and a lot of 
9:275:21686:15:11:90:492:85:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:register based research using Norwegian data is not included. For instance, Roed and Raaum (2003) 
9:276:21784:11:0:90:501:74:10:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f4:*:describe the collection of registers for one research group focusing mainly on labor market outcomes.  
10:277:21887:0:21:126:524:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:There are some common core data sets in all the Nordic countries such as family 
10:278:21967:21:21:90:524:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:links,  several  education  registers  for  test  scores  at  different  levels,  completed  education 
10:279:22070:21:20:90:525:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:etc.,  and  labor  market  outcomes  and  income.  The  countries do,  however,  differ  to  some 
10:280:22168:20:21:90:524:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:degree when  it  comes  to, for  instance, availability  and  access  to  health  data,  vital 
10:281:22261:21:21:90:524:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:statistics, etc. The Nordic countries also differ in terms of how far back in time data sets 
10:282:22352:21:21:90:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:are  linked  and  available  for  potential  research  use.  Of  course,  being  data  collected  for 
10:283:22454:21:20:90:525:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:administrative  purposes,  when  data  are  available  to  study  the  introduction  of  a  given 
10:284:22552:20:21:90:524:564:12:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f3:B:program or policy, it is generally by good fortune rather than prospective design, and it’s 
10:285:22644:21:21:90:422:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:also the case that many policy programs are unique to each country.  
10:286:22712:21:20:126:525:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:In this section we offer three case studies of some of the data potentially available 
10:287:22798:20:21:90:524:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:to  researchers  in  different  jurisdictions,  and  how  they  have  been  used.  Our  case  studies 
10:288:22900:21:21:90:525:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:are  two  Nordic  countries – Norway  and  Sweden – as  well  as  the  state  of Florida.  These 
10:289:22995:21:21:90:525:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:are   not   intended   to   be   complete   overviews,   but   are   rather   examples   of   some 
10:290:23094:21:20:90:524:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:representative uses of administrative registers. When appropriate, we also mention some 
10:291:23181:20:21:90:498:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:complementary work conducted outside of the countries featured in the case studies. 
10:292:23264:21:21:90:93:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:!: 
10:293:23264:42:20:90:144:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:C:A. Norway 
10:294:23273:20:21:125:524:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Most of the research using register based data sets in Norway have exploited the 
10:295:23354:21:21:90:525:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:joint advantages of access to long panels of data combined with parental background and 
10:296:23442:21:20:90:524:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:child  outcomes  along  many  dimensions,  and  the  fact  that  population-wide  data  provides 
10:297:23539:20:21:90:525:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the  opportunity  of  using  policy  reforms  back  in  time  for  identifying  causal  effects.  In 
10:298:23640:21:21:90:524:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:education research, one example of this strategy is assessing the causal effect of parental 
10:299:23732:21:21:90:525:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:education on children education exploiting a mandatory school reform for parents (Black, 
10:300:23821:21:20:90:525:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Devereux and Salvanes, 2005a). In this paper, a parent cohort from the late 1940s to the 
10:301:23909:20:21:90:525:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:late  1950s  and  their  children  are  used  to  estimate  the  intergenerational  transmission  of 
10:302:24010:21:21:90:525:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:education, using the panel structure of the data as well as the family links. In addition, a 
10:303:24103:21:20:90:524:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:mandatory school reform rolled out across 700 municipalities in a period of ten years for 
10:304:24192:20:21:90:524:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the  parental  generation, which is  used  to  identify  the  causal  effect  of  the  educational 
10:305:24289:21:0:90:525:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:transmission  across  generations.  Due  to  the  population  wide  data  set,  the  analysis  could 
11:306:24391:0:21:90:524:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:also  be  undertaken  for  different  education  subgroups, for  instance  whether  mothers  or 
11:307:24487:21:21:90:474:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:fathers or both were affected by the reform, and for different education levels.2  
11:308:24568:21:20:125:524:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Family  links  for  the  whole  population  combined  with  the  long  term  panel 
11:309:24651:20:21:90:524:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:structure following people from birth to adulthood have also been essential in the recent 
11:310:24740:21:21:90:525:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:research using register data in Norway  and the other Nordic countries. Examples of this 
11:311:24829:21:21:90:524:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:line of research is Black, Devereux and Salvanes (2005b, 2007). Both these papers study 
11:312:24917:21:20:90:524:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:family dynamics in the sense of the effect of  family size and birth order,  or child health 
11:313:25010:20:21:90:525:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:on  a  set  of  long  term  outcomes  in  education  and  the  labor  market..  Both  papers  need  to 
11:314:25113:21:21:90:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:match  long  term  outcomes  from  a  large  set  of  registers  measuring  adult  outcomes,  such 
11:315:25212:21:20:90:525:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:as  several  measures  of  education  (years  of  education,  completing  high  school,  college 
11:316:25309:20:21:90:525:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:attendance),  as  well  as  outcomes  in  the  labor  market  including  working  and  annual 
11:317:25403:21:21:90:524:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:earnings. In  Norway,  a  person  register  that  links  family  members  to  one  another  by 
11:318:25498:21:21:90:525:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:relationship  facilitates  the  study  of  questions  such  as birth  order  effects  by  family  size 
11:319:25600:21:20:90:525:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:(Black,  Devereux  and  Salvanes,  2005b).  Black,  Devereux  and  Salvanes  (2007) further 
11:320:25691:20:21:90:524:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:use  a  register  of  twins,  including monozygotic  twins,  to  identify  the  effects child  health 
11:321:25793:21:21:90:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:on long term outcomes. For child health birth weight was used which required merging in 
11:322:25881:21:20:90:525:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the  Norwegian  birth  registry.  Bharadwaj,  Loken  and  Neilson  (2013)  use  a  very  similar 
11:323:25978:20:21:90:524:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:data  set  to  assess  the  effect  on  test  scores  in  school  of  medical  treatment  just  after  birth 
11:324:26087:21:21:90:342:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:for just above or just below very low birth weights.  
11:325:26140:21:20:126:525:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A: Early investment and long term outcomes has been another important part of the 
11:326:26219:20:21:90:524:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:agenda for Norwegian researchers using these data sets – especially using family policies 
11:327:26307:21:21:90:524:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:for  identification.  One  of  the  obvious  advantages of using  the  Norwegian  data  register 
11:328:26402:21:21:90:525:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:data  is  that  since  the  data  goes  long  back,  many  of  the  family  policies  and  education 
11:329:26503:21:20:90:524:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:policies  which were part  of the developing  welfare  state  can  be  analyzed. A  notable 
11:330:26594:20:21:90:525:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:example of this approach is Havnes  and Mogstad (2011) who study the long  run effects 
11:331:26680:21:21:90:525:191:12:g_d0_f3:12:Times New Roman:B:on children’s education and labor market outcomes by exploiting the fact that a day care 
11:332:26769:21:20:90:525:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:reform was rolled out across municipalities in the late 1970s and early 1980s. Similarly, 
11:333:26859:20:21:90:524:150:12:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f3:B:Bettinger,  Haegeland  and  Rege  (2013) investigate a program  that  increased  parents’ 
11:334:26948:21:29:90:525:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:incentives  to  stay  home  with  children  under  the  age  of  three.  They  assess  the  effect  on 
11:335:27051:29:11:234:237:100:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:!:                                                        
11:336:27106:40:15:90:521:89:8:g_d0_f4:10:Times New Roman:D:2 See Bjorklund and Salvanes (2011) for an overview of the international literature on the intergenerational 
11:337:27214:15:0:90:365:74:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:mobility of education, also discussing other identification strategies. 
12:338:27287:0:21:90:524:709:12:g_d0_f3:12:Times New Roman:B:older siblings’ 10th grade GPA, and find support for a positive effect that seems to be 
12:339:27375:21:21:90:524:688:12:g_d0_f3:12:Times New Roman:B:driven by mother’s reduced labor force participation. Another reform used for identifying 
12:340:27464:21:20:90:524:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the  effect  of  even  earlier  investment  in  children  on  adult  outcomes,  is an extension  of a 
12:341:27564:20:21:90:525:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:maternity  leave  program  that  came  into  force  on  July  1,  1977.  This  sharp cutoff  in 
12:342:27660:21:21:90:524:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:eligibility   depending   on   the   exact   date   of   birth   is   well-suited   for   a   regression

12:344:27853:21:20:90:525:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the value of large population-level data is on display, as one requires very large data sets 
12:345:27946:20:21:90:525:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:in  order  to  execute very  data  intensive  non-parametric  approaches.  Interestingly,  fairly 
12:346:28044:21:21:90:524:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:Times New Roman:B:strong effects on children’s medium and long term outcomes were found  for  staying 
12:347:28127:21:20:90:524:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:longer  home  after  birth  with  the  mother.  On  the other  hand,  analyzing extensions  of  the 
12:348:28226:20:21:90:524:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:maternity  leave  reform of up  to  one  year  fully  covered  leave,  and  using  the  same 
12:349:28319:21:21:90:524:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:estimating strategy does not seem to give a positive effect on children’s outcomes (Dahl, 
12:350:28407:21:21:90:525:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Loken, Mogstad and Salvanes, 2013). There clearly seem to be decreasing returns also to 
12:351:28495:21:20:90:327:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:this input in the production function of children.  
12:352:28546:20:21:126:524:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A: Several   other   strategies have been   exploited   to   assess   the   effect   of   early 
12:353:28638:21:21:90:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:investment, especially  related  to  the  effect  of  parental  income, on  in-school  education 
12:354:28733:21:20:90:525:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:outcomes, and a variety  of long-run outcomes. Rege, Telle and Votruba (2011) evaluate 
12:355:28820:20:21:90:524:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the effect on children’s test score in middle school using job loss from mass lay-offs for 
12:356:28910:21:21:90:524:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:identification. They find an asymmetry in the effect of father’s and mother’s job loss – a 
12:357:29000:21:20:90:524:315:12:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f3:B:negative  effect  on  grade  point  average  in  9th grade for father’s job loss and a positive 
12:358:29095:20:21:90:525:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:effect  of  mothers.  The  authors  interpret  their  results  as  not  an  effect  of  income  but  of 
12:359:29199:21:21:90:524:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:distress  form  job  loss  which  is  strongly  negative  for  men. Black,  Devereux,  Loken  and 
12:360:29297:21:21:90:525:253:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Salvanes  (2013)  analyze  the  effect  of  child  care  subsidies  on  children’s  long  term 
12:361:29392:21:20:90:525:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:education using a  sharp  discontinuity  in  the  price  of  childcare  in  Norway.  They  find 
12:362:29486:20:21:90:525:212:12:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f3:B:significant positive effect of the subsidies on children’s middle school performance. This 
12:363:29577:21:21:90:525:191:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:suggest  a  positive  shock  of  disposable  income  on  children’s  school  performance. 
12:364:29667:21:20:90:524:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Carneiro, Lopez-Garcia, Salvanes and Tominey (2014) use very similar data to assess the 
12:365:29755:20:21:90:524:150:12:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f3:B:effect of timing and possible dynamic complementarities of parents income on children’s 
12:366:29842:21:21:90:524:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:short   term   and   long   term   outcomes   both   in   completed years   of education   and 
12:367:29937:21:0:90:522:108:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:performance  in  the  labor  market.  The  rich  data  provides  an  opportunity  to  use  non-
13:368:30034:0:21:90:525:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:parametric methods, and supports findings that not only the discounted life time income 
13:369:30120:21:21:90:494:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:but also timing matter, which supports the dynamic complementarities hypothesis.   
13:370:30198:21:20:126:525:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Since  the  early  2000s  grades  in  high  school  and  middle  school have been 
13:371:30279:20:21:90:524:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:available as well as national tests for some years in primary school. The register of school 
13:372:30372:21:21:90:525:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:grades combined with school resources and information on teachers have been exploited 
13:373:30455:21:21:90:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:to  answer a more  traditional  questions in  the  literature  on  the  economics  of  education. 
13:374:30550:21:20:90:524:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Leuven and Ronning (2011) use grades in middle school to study the effect of class size 
13:375:30638:20:21:90:525:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on students’ achievement exploiting a version of the Maimonides rule, while Haegeland, 
13:376:30725:21:21:90:524:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Kirkeboen,  Raaum  and  Salvanes (2011)  use  the  same  pupil  performance  register,  but  a 
13:377:30820:21:20:90:524:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:wider school resource measure and different identification strategy – a local hydro power 
13:378:30909:20:21:90:525:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:plant  tax.  Both  find  small  effects of  resource  use on  children’s  school performance. 
13:379:31002:21:21:90:524:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Thanks to the  population-wide  register  data  comprising  all  pupils  at  a  grade  level,  peer 
13:380:31101:21:21:90:525:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:effects may be identified. Leuven and Ronning (2014) use the same performance register 
13:381:31188:21:20:90:525:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:but  add  in  detailed  information  on  school  grade  mixing.  They  find  positive  effects  on 
13:382:31287:20:21:90:524:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:pupils  mixed  with  older  peers.  Black,  Devereux  and  Salvanes  (2011)  exploit  this  and 
13:383:31383:21:21:90:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:assess  the  effect  of  the  quality  of  peers  using  within  school  changes  across  years  in  the 
13:384:31488:21:20:90:525:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:composition  of  pupils.  Using  data  going  longer  back  in  time,  they  are  able  to  assess  the 
13:385:31592:20:21:90:525:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:long  term  peer  effects.  In  another  paper,  Black,  Devereux  and  Salvanes  (2013)  analyze 
13:386:31690:21:21:90:525:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the role of school starting age on cognitive outcomes such as IQ tests for boys at age 18, 
13:387:31781:21:20:90:525:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and  for  longer-run  outcomes  such  as  educational  attainment,  teenage  pregnancy,  and 
13:388:31874:20:21:90:524:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:earnings. The important issue in this literature is to separate school starting age from test 
13:389:31968:21:21:90:525:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:age.  Exploiting  variation  in  the  mapping  between  year  and  month  of  birth  and  the  year 
13:390:32068:21:21:90:525:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the military test is taken, allowed the analysis to distinguish the effects of school starting 
13:391:32163:21:20:90:524:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:age  from  pure  age  effects. Findings provide evidence  for  a  very  small  positive  effect  of 
13:392:32262:20:21:90:525:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:starting school younger on IQ scores measured at age 18. In contrast, they find evidence 
13:393:32351:21:21:90:473:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of much larger positive effects of age at test, and these results are very robust.   
13:394:32435:21:20:125:525:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Another  well-studied  area  in  the economics  of education  where  long  panels  of 
13:395:32521:20:21:90:525:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:register  data  may  be  helpful  in  making  progress  is  in  answering  the  seemingly  simple 
13:396:32619:21:21:90:525:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:question  of  what are the  returns  to  education?  Exploiting Norwegian  population  panel 
13:397:32711:21:21:90:525:108:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:data   with   nearly   career   long   earnings   histories,   a   detailed   picture   of   the   causal 
13:398:32817:21:0:90:525:87:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:relationship between schooling and earnings over the life cycle can be analyzed (Bhuller, 
14:399:32909:0:21:90:522:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Mogstad, and Salvanes, 2013). These authors estimate internal rates of returns over life-
14:400:32998:21:21:90:524:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:time  earnings  from  age  17  to the mid-60s  for  many  cohorts, and  make  use  of a  direct 
14:401:33093:21:20:90:524:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:measure of life-time earnings instead of approximating earnings using one year or an age 
14:402:33182:20:21:90:525:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:groups,  and  thus, avoiding  the  problems  of Mincer life-cycle  bias.  When  doing  so,  they 
14:403:33278:21:21:90:455:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:find evidence that the estimated returns to schooling are biased downward.  
14:404:33353:21:21:126:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Administrative  data  have already  been  in  use, in  particular in the  Scandinavian 
14:405:33438:21:20:90:524:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:countries, for  some  years,  and  the  enhanced  knowledge  from  these  studies  have  already 
14:406:33534:20:21:90:525:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:informed  policies  and  we  are  starting  to  see  the  fruits  of  these  new  insights  in  active 
14:407:33637:21:21:90:524:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:policies.  In  Norway,  the  most  striking  example  is a strong  focus that politicians  have 
14:408:33731:21:20:90:525:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:recently put  on  pre-school  or  early  investment  in  children.  As  a  part  of  a  surge  in the 
14:409:33833:20:21:90:525:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:interest   in   early   investment   in   children   and   children   outcomes,   the   focus   among 
14:410:33935:21:21:90:525:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:researchers  in  Norway  has  been  to  exploit  the  possibility  for  assessing  long-term 
14:411:34028:21:21:90:525:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:outcomes in education and the labor market. Both the effect of maternity leave, a daycare 
14:412:34118:21:20:90:525:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:roll  out  for  preschool  children  as  well  as  other  programs  increasing  for  instance  parents 
14:413:34221:20:21:90:524:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:time use in preschool children, have painted quite a consistent picture of the importance 
14:414:34311:21:21:90:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of  early  investment  for  medium  and  long  term  cognitive  outcomes.  These  findings – 
14:415:34403:21:20:90:524:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:together with the international evidence – have informed the public debate and later led to 
14:416:34494:20:21:90:524:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:policy  proving  stronger  incentives  for  more  resource  use  in  for  instance  preschools in 
14:417:34591:21:21:90:525:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Norway. Different from the system in the United States, in the Scandinavian countries the 
14:418:34681:21:20:90:524:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:way  that this  type  of  research  may  penetrate  the  public  debate  and  also  inform  the 
14:419:34776:20:21:90:524:295:12:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f3:B:ministries  and  politicians,  is  mainly  through  forming  groups  of academic “experts” in a 
14:420:34872:21:21:90:524:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:Times New Roman:B:particular area. The “experts” document the new insights from research in the area,  and 
14:421:34959:21:21:90:525:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:write  a  report  to  the  Government.  In  this  case  a  group  of  experts,  including  economists 
14:422:35061:21:20:90:525:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:who  do  research  on  early  investment  using  administrative  data,  drafted a  review  of  the 
14:423:35160:20:21:90:525:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:findings  and  also  came  up  with  concrete  suggestions  for  how  to  improve  both  the 
14:424:35253:21:21:90:524:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:coverage and quality of preschools in Norway (NOU 2010:8). Based on reports like this a 
14:425:35340:21:20:90:525:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:white  paper  will  be  written  to  the  Parliament  with  suggestion  of  a  law  change  or 
14:426:35435:20:21:90:525:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:suggestion for reallocation of money to preschools. There are also several other examples 
14:427:35525:21:21:90:525:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:for  Norway  of how new  research  based  on  administrative  data  informs politicians and 
14:428:35614:21:21:90:524:108:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:leads to  law  changes  outside  the  area  of  education,  for  instance  from  newly  gained 
14:429:35708:21:0:90:323:87:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:information on how the labor market functions.
