15:431:35757:21:21:90:143:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:C:B. Sweden 
15:432:35766:21:20:126:524:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:The Swedish data infrastructure is constructed in a very similar way to Norwegian 
15:433:35848:20:21:90:524:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:data described in the section above. The data comes from local and national registers and 
15:434:35936:21:21:90:525:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:is maintained by municipalities and Statistics Sweden. Each Swedish resident is assigned 
15:435:36024:21:21:90:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:a  unique  and  permanent  identification  number  at  the  time  of  their  birth  and  each 
15:436:36118:21:20:90:525:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:immigrant  is  assigned  a  similar  number  if  they immigrate  to  Sweden  for  more  than  6 
15:437:36214:20:21:90:524:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:months.3 These unique numbers are recorded in every administrative database, be it local 
15:438:36302:21:21:90:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:or national, and allow merging different registers together. They are also used in surveys 
15:439:36392:21:20:90:524:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and experimental studies (Meghir and Palme, 2005; Hinnerich, Hoglin and Johannesson, 
15:440:36476:20:21:90:524:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:2011; Fredriksson, Ockert and Oosterbeek, 2013; Golsteyn, Gronqvist and Lindahl, 2014; 
15:441:36563:21:21:90:260:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Jalava, Joensen and Pellas, 2015)4. 
15:442:36597:21:21:126:524:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Historically  Sweden  conducted  only  population  censuses  at  national  level and 
15:443:36681:21:20:90:525:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:maintained birth and death records at parish level. Similar to Norway, this changed in the 
15:444:36772:20:21:90:525:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:1960s  when  Statistics  Sweden  (SCB)  started  building  their  registry  data.  Today  SCB 
15:445:36866:21:21:90:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:maintains  four  core  registers  that  together  contain  more  than  50  different  thematically 
15:446:36965:21:20:90:524:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:focused  sub-registers.  These  four  core  data  sets  cover  population  (e.g.  employment  or 
15:447:37062:20:21:90:525:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:education  registers),  activity  (e.g.  earnings  or  pupils  registers),  real  estate  (e.g.  prices  or 
15:448:37170:21:21:90:524:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:GIS  registers)  and  business  (e.g.  patent  or  schools  registers). In  addition  to  these  SCB 
15:449:37270:21:20:90:525:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:registers, the National Board of Health and Welfare maintains more than 70 registers with 
15:450:37360:20:21:90:524:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:individual  level  medical  diagnoses5.  The  registers  are  accessible  to  research  community 
15:451:37458:21:21:90:524:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:through Statistics  Sweden,  various  research  institutes  (e.g.,  the  Research  Institute  in 
15:452:37555:21:21:90:525:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Industrial Economics, or IFN) or governmental agencies (e.g., the Institute for Evaluation 
15:453:37645:21:20:90:524:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of Labour Market in Education Policy, or IFAU). Access is granted on project-by-project 
15:454:37732:20:21:90:525:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:basis  and  each  application  undergoes  detailed  investigation.  Different  registers  are 
15:455:37826:21:21:90:525:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:merged  by  SCB  and  researchers  obtain  data  sets  with  a  new  unique,  but  randomly 
15:456:37918:21:27:90:251:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:generated, individual identifiers.  
15:457:37953:27:7:234:237:143:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:!:                                                        
15:458:38008:34:16:90:503:136:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:3 When the system was created in the 1960s all the living Swedes were also assigned unique identifiers 
15:459:38110:16:7:90:156:120:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:retrospectively.  
15:460:38127:7:16:90:512:113:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:4 Jalava, Joensen and Pellas (2015) evaluate short term effects of experimental intervention in Stockholm 
15:461:38232:16:7:90:478:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:schools, and their subsequent research will merge in registry data to study longer-run outcomes.  
15:462:38328:7:16:90:486:90:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:5 Similar data exist in a number of locations including Manitoba (Currie et al., 2010) and Denmark 
15:463:38423:16:0:90:262:74:10:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:*:(Dalsgaard, Nielsen and Simonsen, 2014). 
16:464:38465:0:21:126:525:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Due   to   security   and   data   management   reasons   SCB   maintains   different 
16:465:38551:21:21:90:524:688:12:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f3:B:educational databases under different “big registers”, and hence for a given project these 
16:466:38642:21:20:90:525:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:need  to  be  merged  with  one  another.  For  instance,  Fredriksson,  Ockert  and  Oosterbeek 
16:467:38739:20:21:90:525:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:(2013) investigate the long-run effects of class size, and their baseline data set is actually 
16:468:38833:21:21:90:524:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:a purpose-built  longitudinal  survey  run  by  the  Department  of  Education  at  Gothenburg 
16:469:38927:21:21:90:524:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:University.  However,  since  the  subjects in this  survey  all  have  unique  identification 
16:470:39021:21:20:90:525:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:numbers  it  is  possible  to  link  them  back  to  other  administrative  data  sources.  In 
16:471:39116:20:21:90:525:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:particular,  the  authors  add  data  on  class  size  from  class  registers,  parental  information 
16:472:39218:21:21:90:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:from  multigenerational  registers,  medium-term  achievement  from  compulsory  school 
16:473:39306:21:20:90:524:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:pupil registers and military draft registers, completed education from education registers, 
16:474:39397:20:21:90:525:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:earnings from statement of earnings registers and wages from wages and staff for public 
16:475:39484:21:21:90:524:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and   private   sector registers.   On   the   one   hand,   this   decomposition   illustrates   the 
16:476:39585:21:21:90:525:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:complexity  of  the  data  structure  and  emphasizes  the  crucial  role  of  unique  personal 
16:477:39681:21:20:90:524:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:identifier. On the other hand, such a complex structure enhances the security of the very 
16:478:39771:20:21:90:448:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:sensitive personal information and improves the management of the data.  
16:479:39843:21:21:126:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:The  long  panels  and  retrospective  assignment  of  unique  individual  identifiers 
16:480:39930:21:20:90:525:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:allow studying lifecycle and multigenerational effects also in the case of Sweden. Meghir 
16:481:40020:20:21:90:525:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and Palme (2005) study the effects of comprehensive schooling reform that among other 
16:482:40106:21:21:90:525:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:elements  increased  the  length  of  compulsory  schooling,  and  was  introduced  in  the  late 
16:483:40204:21:20:90:525:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:1940s. They utilize survey data on two cohorts that are then linked to registry data which 
16:484:40294:20:21:90:525:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:provide  individual  educational  attainment  and  earnings.  Meghir,  Palme  and  Schnabel 
16:485:40386:21:21:90:525:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:(2012)  utilize  the  same  reform,  richer  data  set and  show  that  it  not  only  reduces  the 
16:486:40485:21:21:90:524:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:criminal  activity of  the  treated  generation  but  also  of  their  children.  Even  more  data 
16:487:40583:21:20:90:525:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:demanding  endeavor  is  undertaken  by  Palme  et  al.  (2015)  where  they  combine  Swedish 
16:488:40678:20:21:90:525:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:registers  and  historical  survey  records  to  estimate  the  intergenerational  persistence  of 
16:489:40777:21:21:90:465:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:human capital, measured by educational attainment, across four generations.   
16:490:40854:21:20:126:524:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Both  Norway  and  Sweden  share  two  very  unique  and  purpose  built  data  sets: 
16:491:40940:20:21:90:522:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:military assessment and adoptions. The former one provides physical, cognitive and non-
16:492:41027:21:0:90:525:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:cognitive  assessment  of  all  males  at  the  age  of  18-19  (Lundborg,  Nilsson  and  Rooth, 
17:493:41126:0:21:90:524:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:2014)6. The latter one contains all persons who were born in Sweden between 1962 and 
17:494:41211:21:21:90:524:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:1996  and  adopted  by  both  parents  (Bjorklund,  Lindahl  and  Plug,  2006;  Holmlund, 
17:495:41301:21:20:90:525:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Lindahl  and  Plug,  2011)7.  Together  with  the  ability  to  link  these  data  to  population 
17:496:41399:20:21:90:525:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:registers they provide social scientists with extremely powerful analytical tool. There are 
17:497:41491:21:21:90:525:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:also  several  other  purpose  built  survey  data  sets  in  Sweden.  Fredriksson,  Ockert  and 
17:498:41588:21:21:90:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Oosterbeek  (2013)  use the Gothenburg  University panel  mentioned  above containing 
17:499:41672:21:20:90:525:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:cognitive  test  scores  for  13  year  olds.  Golsteyn,  Gronqvist  and  Lindahl  (2014)  use the 
17:500:41771:20:21:90:524:564:12:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f3:B:Stockholm   Birth   Cohort   Study,   which contains  information  on  children’s  time 
17:501:41859:21:21:90:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:preferences at age 13. In the paper the authors link this survey to administrative data and 
17:502:41950:21:20:90:524:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:conclude  that  adolescent  time  preferences  predict  outcomes  up  to  five  decades later  in 
17:503:42047:20:21:90:111:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:life. 
17:504:42052:21:21:126:525:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Although Sweden, and likewise Norway and Denmark, seem like ideal places for 
17:505:42129:21:21:90:524:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:empirical studies on the intersection of family, health, education and labor markets, there 
17:506:42221:21:20:90:525:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:are still many challenges in carrying out this research in reality. The two main obstacles 
17:507:42311:20:21:90:525:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:in  educational  research are  that  authorities  tend  to  be  reluctant  to  allow  the  conduct  of 
17:508:42414:21:21:90:524:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:field  experiments,  as  well  as  the  lack  of  longitudinal  assessment  data.  Scandinavia, 
17:509:42510:21:20:90:525:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:including  Sweden, lags  far  behind the  United  States in  the  implementation  of  the  field 
17:510:42604:20:21:90:525:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:experiments  related  to  student  incentives  (Fryer,  2014),  student  support  (Cook  et  al., 
17:511:42702:21:21:90:525:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:2014),  teacher  incentives  (Imberman  and  Lovenheim, 2015),  school  choice  (Deming  et 
17:512:42794:21:20:90:525:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:al.,  2014)  or  school  management  (Fryer, 2014).  Given  the  problems  with  tracking 
17:513:42884:20:21:90:524:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:students   over   time   in   the   United   States,   the   Scandinavian   administrative   data 
17:514:42982:21:21:90:524:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:infrastructure is ideal to study long-run consequences and potential positive and negative 
17:515:43073:21:21:90:525:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:spillovers  of  policy  interventions,  and  field  experiments  are  current  gold  standard  in 
17:516:43171:21:20:90:182:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:policy evaluation.  
17:517:43190:20:21:126:525:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:That said, the Scandinavian countries do have a fair degree of assessment data of 
17:518:43272:21:21:90:525:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:late. Sweden, similar to  Denmark  and Norway, introduced in  recent  years some form of 
17:519:43361:21:20:90:524:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:longitudinal  assessments  in  their  compulsory  schools.  The  longitudinal  assessment  data 
17:520:43457:20:30:90:525:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:in Sweden began in 2009 and comprise of tests  given in  grades three, six and nine. The 
17:521:43546:30:7:234:237:120:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:!:                                                        
17:522:43601:37:16:90:519:113:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:6 Since the mid 2000s the draft is no longer mandatory in Sweden so the data does not provide information 
17:523:43705:16:12:90:499:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:on the whole population. The draft continues to be mandatory in Norway. Finland has also mandatory 
17:524:43804:12:7:90:303:85:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:military draft (Kerr, Pekkarinen and Uusitalo, 2013). 
17:525:43857:7:0:90:356:78:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:7 The register is now expanded to cover more recent birth cohorts. 
18:526:43924:0:21:90:525:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:assessment data in grades 3 and 6 have not been widely used in research thus far8. Before 
18:527:44014:21:21:90:524:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:this reform Swedish students were only assessed at the age 16. These data on compulsory 
18:528:44102:21:20:90:525:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:school  exit  exams  are  available  since  1988,  and  have  been  often  used,  for  example  by 
18:529:44201:20:21:90:525:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Almond,  Edlund  and  Palme  (2009)  who  study  the  effects  of  prenatal  exposure  to 
18:530:44291:21:21:90:525:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:radioactive fallout on school outcomes. It is worth noting that unlike in the United States 
18:531:44382:21:21:90:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:all  tests  in  Scandinavian  countries  are  low  stakes  and  the  Swedish  Education  Agency 
18:532:44478:21:20:90:525:584:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:explicitly states that they “... are not examination, but should be part of the teacher 
18:533:44566:20:21:90:524:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:Times New Roman:B:information about student’s knowledge...” In  fact,  except  for  Stockholm  and  Malmo, 
18:534:44655:21:21:90:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:these  virtually  do  not  matter  for  high  school  admissions  as  children  are  guaranteed  a 
18:535:44754:21:20:90:347:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:place in their closest high school (Karbownik, 2014). 
18:536:44807:20:21:126:524:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Sweden  and  Denmark,  unlike  Norway,  have  also  implemented  a  large-scale 
18:537:44887:21:21:90:524:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:refugee  placement  policy  in  a  nearly  random  way.  The  placement  assignment  could  be 
18:538:44982:21:21:90:525:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:seen as random conditional on observables because the individual could not choose their 
18:539:45070:21:20:90:525:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:first  place  of  residence  and  there  was  no  direct  interaction  between  a  refugee  and 
18:540:45166:20:21:90:524:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:placement  officers.  This  does  not  guarantee  that  immigrants  were  randomly  assigned  to 
18:541:45263:21:21:90:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:neighborhoods,  in  fact  they  were  not,  but  the  placement  selection  was  based  on 
18:542:45354:21:20:90:525:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:observable attributes of immigrants and these are all available in administrative data. This 
18:543:45447:20:21:90:524:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:policy  has  been  extensively  studied  not  only  for  its  labor  market  consequences  for 
18:544:45542:21:21:90:525:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:immigrants themselves (Edin, Fredriksson and Aslund, 2003) but also for the educational 
18:545:45630:21:20:90:348:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:consequences of their children (Aslund et al., 2011)9. 
18:546:45684:20:21:126:525:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Sweden  is  also  the  only  one  of  the Scandinavian  countries  that  introduced  some 
18:547:45773:21:21:90:525:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:form of charter schools. Unlike in the US these have not been introduced with a random 
18:548:45860:21:21:90:524:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:component   and   allow   only   for   differences-in-differences   type   of   identification. 
18:549:45956:21:20:90:525:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Sandstrom  and  Bergsrton  (2005)  study  the  effects  of  the  reform,  and  the  competition  it 
18:550:46056:20:21:90:525:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:induces,  on  quality  of  public  schools.  Bohlmark  and  Lindahl  (2015)  study  its  long-run 
18:551:46154:21:21:90:525:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:consequences.  Hensvik  (2012)  utilized  the  same  reform  to  understand  how  competition 
18:552:46248:21:27:90:525:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:affects  teacher  mobility  and  wages.  Wikstrom  and  Wikstrom  (2005)  document  that 
18:553:46337:27:7:234:237:143:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:!:                                                        
18:554:46392:34:16:90:523:136:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:8 Raw scores are not kept by the authorities and for the early schooling test it is only the pass/fail indicator 
18:555:46504:16:12:90:524:120:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:that is recorded in the registers. Although, from research perspective the more continuous score measure is 
18:556:46611:12:11:90:524:108:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:very valuable this is a clear example  where the research needs do not cross with the administrative  needs, 
18:557:46720:11:7:90:496:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:and indeed this data serves primarily administrative purposes for which a binary coding is sufficient.  
18:558:46821:7:16:90:517:90:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:9 The Danish study uses the placement policy to study the effects of early exposure to neighborhood crime 
18:559:46926:16:0:90:395:74:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:on subsequent criminal behavior of the youth (Damm and Dustmann, 2014) 
19:560:46998:0:21:90:525:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:school  competition  leads  to  grade  inflation,  and  that  voucher  schools  inflate  their 
19:561:47093:21:21:90:525:688:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:students’ grades more heavily. Sweden has also introduced two other market oriented 
19:562:47177:21:20:90:525:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:educational  reforms  that  have  been  evaluated  by  researchers.  The  first  transferred  the 
19:563:47275:20:21:90:525:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:funding responsibilities from central government to local municipalities (Fredriksson and 
19:564:47365:21:21:90:525:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Ockert,  2008).  The  second  allowed  individual  level  wage  bargaining  between  teachers 
19:565:47459:21:21:90:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and  principals  (Bohlmark,  Gronqvist  and  Vlachos, 2012).  Yet  another  school  choice 
19:566:47549:21:20:90:525:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:reform  was  introduced  in  Stockholm  in  2000,  and  changed  the  high  school  admission 
19:567:47643:20:21:90:525:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:system  from  one  largely  based  on  place  of  residence  to  another  entirely  based  on 
19:568:47737:21:21:90:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:compulsory school performance i.e. change from zoning to open enrollment. Soderstrom 
19:569:47822:21:20:90:525:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and   Uusitalo   (2010)   document   that   the   reform   lead   to   sharp   changes   in   student 
19:570:47924:20:21:90:525:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:composition in Stockholm schools, while Karbownik (2014) shows that these changes in 
19:571:48009:21:21:90:356:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:student quality lead to changes in teacher labor supply. 
19:572:48065:21:21:90:93:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:!: 
19:573:48065:42:20:90:143:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:C:C. Florida 
19:574:48075:20:21:126:525:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Due to the decentralized nature of education in the United States, there exists no 
19:575:48158:21:21:90:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:prospect of national educational data records, at least in the foreseeable future. However, 
19:576:48250:21:20:90:525:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:a number of states and school districts have established systems in which students can be 
19:577:48340:20:21:90:525:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:followed  longitudinally  and  matched  to  schools  and,  in  some  cases,  their  teachers  over 
19:578:48439:21:21:90:524:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:time.  The  three  states  with  the  longest-standing  state  level  student  longitudinal  data 
19:579:48537:21:20:90:525:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:systems  that  have  been  widely  available  for  researchers  are  Florida,  North  Carolina  and 
19:580:48637:20:21:90:124:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Texas. 
19:581:48643:21:21:126:525:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A: Florida   has   maintained   statewide   records   of   student   test   scores   that   are 
19:582:48736:21:21:90:525:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:longitudinally  comparable  (initially  in  grades  4,  5,  8,  and  10,  and  soon  thereafter 
19:583:48832:21:20:90:525:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:expanded  to  grades  3  through  10)  since  the  1997-98  school  year  within  its Education 
19:584:48928:20:21:90:525:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Data Warehouse (EDW). The EDW also includes information on high school graduation, 
19:585:49011:21:21:90:525:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:grade  retention,  student  attendance,  disciplinary  infractions,  school  assignments,  home 
19:586:49107:21:20:90:524:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:language,  immigrant  status,  disability,  race/ethnicity,  gender,  school  transcripts,  and  a 
19:587:49206:20:21:90:525:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:measure  of  student  poverty,  along  with  other  measures.  Florida  assigns  a  unique

21:651:55007:37:16:90:507:113:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:11 These data sets are linked by name, date of birth, and social security number (a national identification 
21:652:55114:16:12:90:513:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:number). This three-factor linkage allows for much more accurate matching of data across administrative

22:655:55360:0:21:90:525:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:population; and Black et al. (2014) identify the effects of disabled siblings by comparing

22:662:55953:20:21:126:525:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A: These  Florida  data  provide  some  distinct  advantages  over data  sets  observed  in

22:681:57787:21:20:90:525:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:shortcomings   of   matched   birth   and   school   records   in   the   United   States   context.

22:684:58082:21:0:90:265:108:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:United States and around the world. 
23:685:58119:0:21:126:524:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A: As  in  the  Scandinavian  context,  research  using  administrative  data  from  Florida 
23:686:58209:21:21:90:525:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:has led to substantial policy changes. Noteworthy examples include how school voucher

23:691:58676:21:20:90:525:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:research  identified  the  degree  to  which  the  attainment  of  this  credential  influenced – or 
23:692:58776:20:21:90:524:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:failed to influence – teacher performance in the classroom. These examples, coupled with

23:701:59498:42:20:90:406:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:C:IV. Challenges associated with the use of administrative data  
23:702:59559:20:21:125:525:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:We  have  so  far  stressed  the  important  advantages of administrative  registers as 
23:703:59644:21:21:90:525:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:compared  to  survey  data - fewer  issues  with  recall  and  other  measurement problems; 
23:704:59733:21:20:90:525:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:since  its population-wide  the  data  set  is  representative; less  problems  with  attrition 
23:705:59827:20:21:90:525:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:compared  to surveys  that  follow  the  sampled  populations  over  time; less  problems  with 
23:706:59921:21:21:90:524:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:non-response;  and  the  ability  to  study  heterogeneous  effects  and  rare  and  infrequent 
23:707:60017:21:21:90:525:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:events.  Combined  with  data  for  public  policies  in  the  past,  many  credible  policy 
23:708:60110:21:20:90:525:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:evaluations  such  as  education  policies  and  family  policies  as  described  above  can  be 
23:709:60207:20:21:90:525:212:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:analyzed. Complete family links makes it possible to exploit other “experiments” for 
23:710:60292:21:21:90:524:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:identification  such  as  comparing  siblings  and  twins  as  well as  the  use  of  adoptees.  The 
23:711:60393:21:20:90:525:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:long  panel  structure  of  administrative  registers  makes  it  possible  to  assess  the  effects of 
23:712:60496:20:21:90:525:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:policy  programs  both  for  short  and  long  terms  outcomes  across  a  large  number  of 
23:713:60589:21:0:90:331:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:outcomes and across many administrative unites.  
24:714:60638:0:21:125:524:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:However,  there  are  certain  limitations  or  restrictions  related  to  the  use  of 
24:715:60726:21:21:90:525:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:administrative  register  data,  and  we  try  to  distinguish  between  three  different  aspects  of 
24:716:60829:21:20:90:470:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:restrictions as compared to surveys designed for particular research questions.  
24:717:60909:20:21:125:128:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:!: 
24:718:60909:41:21:108:449:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:C:A. Limited information/less flexibility than with purpose-built surveys 
24:719:60979:21:21:108:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Administrative  registers  are  collected  for  different  reasons  than  research,  and  in 
24:720:61072:21:20:90:524:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:particular in one  area they have limitations  as  compared  to  purpose-built  surveys.  Very 
24:721:61165:20:21:90:525:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:little information on cognitive skills other than achievement and attainment or social and 
24:722:61255:21:21:90:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:behavioral skills  are  available  in  most  register  data.  Variables  that  potentially  are  very 
24:723:61356:21:20:90:525:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:important  in  understanding  for  instance  school  choices  such  as  motivation  and  attitudes 
24:724:61455:20:21:90:525:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and  more general  psychological  traits  for  instance  as  measured  by  Big  five  components 
24:725:61551:21:21:90:524:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:are not available. Some of these questions are available in some countries in military data 
24:726:61643:21:21:90:366:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:for men, but usually only for a limited number of years.   
24:727:61701:21:20:125:525:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:This lack of important information on, for instance, reasons for education choices 
24:728:61782:20:21:90:525:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:or  effort  is  a  challenge,  but  several  new  strategies  are  being  used  to  mediate  this 
24:729:61880:21:21:90:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:limitation.  Several  research  groups  in  the  Nordic  countries  are  now  combining  surveys 
24:730:61977:21:20:90:524:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:with  registers  data,  as  well  as  lab  experiments  and  randomized  field  experiments  with 
24:731:62075:20:21:90:157:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:register data.  
24:732:62090:21:21:125:525:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:One  example  connected  to  the  economics  of  education  undertaken is in  Norway, 
24:733:62175:21:20:90:524:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:where pupils just prior to the decision to attend  high school, were surveyed on the “Big 
24:734:62262:20:21:90:525:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:five” personality traits and on the information about the labor market (Almas, Cappelen, 
24:735:62349:21:21:90:524:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Salvanes,  Sorensen,  Tungodden,  2014). The  idea  in  the  project  was  to  use  incentivized 
24:736:62445:21:21:90:525:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:lab experiments to tease out preferences for willingness to compete, risk taking, patience 
24:737:62536:21:20:90:525:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:etc., together  with  an  ability  test,  a  survey  regarding the “big  five”,  time  use  on 
24:738:62631:20:21:90:524:212:12:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f3:B:homework  etc., and a quite intensive survey on the students’ knowledge of the labor 
24:739:62715:21:21:90:525:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:market  and  the  returns  to  education.  Parents  and  students  provided  consent to  follow 
24:740:62810:21:20:90:524:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:these  students  through  the  education  system  and  into  the  labor  market,  and  to  match  to 
24:741:62911:20:21:90:524:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:parental background from register data. Many research questions may be analyzed using 
24:742:62997:21:21:90:525:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:this  resource, for  instance  to  better  understand  high  drop-out  rates.  These  type  of 
24:743:63092:21:0:90:524:108:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:approach  also facilitates field  experiments  in  school,  and  then allows following pupils 
25:744:63186:0:21:90:525:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:through the education system, into the labor market. Hence, the lack of information in the 
25:745:63277:21:21:90:396:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:administrative data sets may be compensated in different ways. 
25:746:63339:21:20:125:128:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:!: 
25:747:63339:41:21:108:398:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:C:B. Technical issues with the use of administrative registers 
25:748:63398:21:21:125:525:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Depending on the country, issues of a more technical nature might be an obstacle 
25:749:63478:21:21:90:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:in  the  use  of  administrative  registers.  One  such obstacle is  the  ability  to  match 
25:750:63570:21:20:90:524:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:administrative  registers  across  administrative units.  For  instance,  important  research 
25:751:63663:20:21:90:524:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:topics  can  be  analyzed by connecting school  outcomes  to  long  term  outcomes  such  as 
25:752:63753:21:21:90:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:income and completed education, or even outcomes such as fertility, crime, and marriage. 
25:753:63842:21:20:90:525:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:In  many  countries,  and  notably  the  Nordic  countries  a  common identification number  is 
25:754:63936:20:21:90:525:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:utilized  across  all  administrative  units  and  across  all  registers.  Furthermore,  even  if  the 
25:755:64040:21:21:90:525:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:different  administrative  registers  are  collected  and  owned  in  principle  by  the  different 
25:756:64140:21:21:90:524:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:units, a law for statistical usage for research purposes enables researchers to use merged 
25:757:64231:21:20:90:525:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:registers  across  administrative  units.  De-identified  and  merged  data are made  available 
25:758:64326:20:21:90:525:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:through   the   national statistical   offices. But   in many   countries   a   unique   personal 
25:759:64423:21:21:90:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:identification number either does not exist, or there are legal restrictions to merge across 
25:760:64516:21:20:90:524:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:administrative  units12. For  example,  in  the  United  States  only  a  few  states  have  linked 
25:761:64616:20:21:90:525:357:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:children’s social security numbers, which are used for all labor market and benefits data, 
25:762:64707:21:21:90:524:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:to  their  birth  records,  and  in  many  states  it  is  actually  illegal  to  link  social  security 
25:763:64812:21:20:90:525:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:numbers  to  education  records.  In  cases  like  these,  it  becomes  extremely  difficult  to  link 
25:764:64915:20:21:90:525:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:data  across  administrative  data  domains.  While  many  states  in  the  United  States  are 
25:765:65011:21:21:90:525:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:making strong progress in linking education and workforce data, thanks to the leadership 
25:766:65100:21:21:90:524:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of  the  Data  Quality  Campaign,  a  national  organization  dedicated  to  promoting  the 
25:767:65192:21:20:90:525:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:development, implementation, and use of high-quality administrative education data sets, 
25:768:65279:20:21:90:409:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and other allied groups, this is a difficult and slow-going process.  
25:769:65348:21:21:125:524:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Another  issue  is, of  course, that  it  is  hard  to  follow people moving  to  other 
25:770:65433:21:20:90:524:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:countries since they may change citizenship, or even if people are studying and working 
25:771:65520:20:21:90:524:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:abroad  it  is  hard  to follow  them  in  terms  of  income  or  graduation.  Hence,  attrition  of 
25:772:65621:21:32:90:525:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:samples might be an issue. One will be able to identify which country they move to and 
25:773:65708:32:7:234:237:97:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:!:                                                        
25:774:65763:39:16:90:484:90:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:12 Another legal restriction was in place, until recently, in Finland where the possibility of indirect 
25:775:65866:16:0:90:522:74:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:identification of individuals in small groups prevented researchers from using registry data in full capacity.  
26:776:65979:0:21:90:525:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the  reason  for  moving,  but  not  outcomes.  This  is  of  course  a  limitation,  but  the  same 
26:777:66080:21:21:90:524:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:limitation is shared by standard surveys. This issue is certainly compounded in countries 
26:778:66169:21:20:90:525:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:like the United States where people move freely  and often between states but individual 
26:779:66258:20:21:90:525:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:states maintain their own birth records, health records, education records, and workforce 
26:780:66348:21:21:90:524:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:data. In  recent  years,  it  has  become  possible  in  rare  circumstances  to  match  school 
26:781:66443:21:21:90:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:records to tax data from the Internal Revenue Service in order to follow children living in 
26:782:66535:21:20:90:525:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:one  state  to  adult  outcomes  in  another  state  (see,  e.g.,  Chetty  et  al.,  2014),  and  we are 
26:783:66639:20:21:90:364:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:hopeful that more cases like that will occur in the future. 
26:784:66698:21:21:125:524:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Since the administrative  data sets  are not designed for  research in the  first place, 
26:785:66787:21:20:90:524:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:they  are  not particularly well-documented  (with  some  exceptions).  This  also  means  that 
26:786:66882:20:21:90:524:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:there  is  a  big  investment  aspect  of  using  these  data  sets  as  compared  to  more  standard 
26:787:66984:21:21:90:525:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:surveys, for instance in the United States some of the surveys are publicly available and 
26:788:67071:21:21:90:525:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:very  well  documented.  The  larger  research  groups  in  the  Nordic  countries  using  several 
26:789:67170:21:20:90:525:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:matched  registers  have  used  the  data  sets  over  a  long  time  and  spent  a  considerable 
26:790:67268:20:21:90:525:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:amount  of  resources  in  checking  the  data  and  understanding its structure,  the  content  of 
26:791:67366:21:21:90:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the variables, and the changing definitions of these variables over time. Due to changes in 
26:792:67458:21:20:90:525:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:tax  laws  for  instance,  also  the  definition  of  earnings  provided  in  these  data  sets  may 
26:793:67559:20:21:90:525:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:change.  These  changes  are  not  always  easily  available  to  outsiders  of  the administrative 
26:794:67659:21:21:90:524:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:units collecting the data. And of course, it is always possible that the administrative data 
26:795:67752:21:20:90:525:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:sets  are  incomplete  or  have  other  errors  in  them,  because  their  purpose  was  never  for 
26:796:67852:20:21:90:524:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:research  quality  but  rather  for  recording  activities  such  as  governmental  program 
26:797:67944:21:21:90:525:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:participation and compliance. As a consequence, these data may not have been subjected 
26:798:68031:21:21:90:525:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:to  the  same  type  of  quality  assurance/quality  control  that  is  standard  in  the  case  of  data 
26:799:68137:21:20:90:324:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:sets collected specifically for research purposes. 
26:800:68187:20:21:125:128:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:!: 
26:801:68187:41:21:90:282:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:C:C. Political issues related to anonymity 
26:802:68227:21:20:125:525:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:An important issue with using administrative registers is that they cannot be made 
26:803:68308:20:21:90:525:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:available  publicly,  due  to  security  and  confidentiality  concerns.  Given  that  unique 
26:804:68402:21:21:90:524:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:personal  identifiers  exist,  most  countries  with  these  data  sets  have  developed  secure 
26:805:68499:21:21:90:525:108:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:systems  for  making  them  available  to  researchers  or  research  groups.  In  the  Nordic 
26:806:68594:21:0:90:525:87:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:countries  (with  the  exception  of  Finland  where  a  slightly  different  system  is  in  place), 
27:807:68698:0:21:90:524:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:very similar system have been developed over time where the Statistical agencies play an 
27:808:68786:21:21:90:524:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:important  role  in  merging  and  de-identifying  data  for  researchers, generally through 
27:809:68879:21:20:90:525:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:research centers that have been through a quite extensive application procedure with data 
27:810:68967:20:21:90:389:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:authorities, owners of data and the national statistical offices.  
27:811:69033:21:21:125:524:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:For all of the Nordic countries there are several research groups with access to the 
27:812:69118:21:21:90:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:same  or  very  overlapping  collection  of  administrative  data  sets,  and  no  research  group 
27:813:69217:21:20:90:524:584:12:g_d0_f3:12:Times New Roman:B:has the “monopoly” to certain registers. The advantage is, of course, that research can be 
27:814:69306:20:21:90:524:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:replicated by other researchers. This is true to an increasing degree in a number of other 
27:815:69397:21:21:90:524:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:countries,  such  as  the  United  Kingdom,  Chile,  the  Netherlands,  and  numerous states  in 
27:816:69494:21:20:90:525:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the US,  to  name  a  few.  Governments  must  balance  the  costs  associated  with  potential 
27:817:69590:20:21:90:525:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:security breaches against the very large benefits of making data available to a wide range 
27:818:69681:21:21:90:525:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of  researchers,  who  have  insights  and  expertise  in  a  larger  set  of  substantive  research 
27:819:69782:21:21:90:524:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:issues. It   is imperative   that   researchers   work   diligently   to   ensure   that   they   treat 
27:820:69885:21:20:90:525:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:administrative  data  with  care  and  maintain  high  degree  of  security  so  that  justifiably 
27:821:69984:20:21:90:525:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:worried  stewards  of  administrative  data  can  feel  more  confident  that  sharing  data  with 
27:822:70083:21:21:90:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:scholars provides high benefits to citizens with extremely low risks of security breaches 
27:823:70173:21:20:90:270:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:or other forms of negligent behavior. 
27:824:70210:20:21:125:128:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:!: 
27:825:70210:41:21:90:359:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:C:V. The use of administrative data around the world  
27:826:70260:21:20:126:525:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:We begin this section by specifying different types of administrative data used in 
27:827:70343:20:21:90:524:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:educational  research.  In  tables 1 through  4 we  mostly  focus  on  student  or  teacher 
27:828:70433:21:21:90:525:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:registries; however, we also consider principals, pre-formal schooling children and other 
27:829:70522:21:21:90:525:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:individuals  for  whom  we  observe  administrative  educational  records. These  tables  are 
27:830:70615:21:20:90:525:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:divided by whether the data sets are matched or unmatched to other records, and whether 
27:831:70703:20:21:90:524:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:or  not  they  are  linked  to surveys  or experiments. Table  1  lists  papers  that  use  a  single 
27:832:70805:21:21:90:525:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:administrative  data  source;  table  2  lists  papers  that  matches  individuals  across  various 
27:833:70905:21:20:90:525:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:administrative  data  sources;  table  3  lists  papers  that  use  a  single  administrative  data 
27:834:71005:20:21:90:525:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:source  which  is  matched  to  either  survey  or  experimental  data;  table  4  lists  papers  that 
27:835:71108:21:21:90:524:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:matches individuals both across various administrative data sources and to either survey 
27:836:71197:21:21:90:525:108:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:or  experiment. We  group  the  papers  by  continent,  country,  region  (state)  and  provide 
27:837:71293:21:0:90:281:87:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:abbreviated bibliographic information.  
28:838:71334:0:21:126:525:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:It is not our purpose to provide an encyclopedic review of all papers making use 
28:839:71415:21:21:90:525:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of  administrative  data  around the  world,  but  we  wanted  to  offer  a  very  wide-ranging 
28:840:71510:21:20:90:525:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:sampling of the current state of the use of administrative data throughout the world. We 
28:841:71599:20:21:90:524:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:therefore  sought to  systematically  survey  a  large  number  of  leading  economics  outlets 
28:842:71695:21:21:90:525:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:that  publish  papers  in  the economics  of  education.  Specifically,  we browsed  all  articles 
28:843:71793:21:21:90:524:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:published  or  accepted  for  publication  between January 1990  and  July  2014  in  the 
28:844:71883:21:20:90:524:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:American   Economic   Journal:   Applied   Economics, American   Economic   Journal: 
28:845:71968:20:21:90:525:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Economic   Policy, American   Economic   Review, Econometrica, Economic   Journal, 
28:846:72048:21:21:90:524:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Economics  of  Education  Review, Education  Finance  and  Policy, Journal  of  Human 
28:847:72133:21:20:90:524:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Resources, Journal of Labor Economics, Journal of Political Economy, Journal of Public 
28:848:72220:20:21:90:524:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Economics, Quarterly Journal of Economics, Review of Economic Studies, and Review of 
28:849:72304:21:21:90:525:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Economics and Statistics, as well as all 2014 NBER Working Papers from the Education 
28:850:72389:21:21:90:525:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:program published until the end of July 2014. Although we recognize that this list is far 
28:851:72479:21:20:90:525:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:from  being comprehensive,  we  covered  350  papers  from  28  countries  and  all  continents 
28:852:72575:20:21:90:200:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:except for Antarctica.  
28:853:72598:21:21:126:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:In  the  tables,  we organize  countries  by  regions  of  the  world -- Europe,  North 
28:854:72684:21:20:90:524:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:America,  South  America,  Asia, Africa,  and Oceania – and then  order  all  papers  within 
28:855:72775:20:21:90:525:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:country  and  state  (region)  by  publication  date13. It  is  clear  that  the  majority  of  research 
28:856:72880:21:21:90:525:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:(published in these outlets at least) makes use of data from North America (253 papers), 
28:857:72969:21:20:90:524:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and  in  particular the United  States  (240  papers). It  is  possible  that  this  is  a  substantial 
28:858:73073:20:21:90:524:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:overstatement  of the  North  American  share  of  education  economics  research  using 
28:859:73162:21:21:90:525:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:administrative data because of possible publication biases of the journals that we selected 
28:860:73254:21:21:90:525:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:for  inclusion,  but  again,  our  charge  is  not  to  be  comprehensive  in  our  survey.  A  large 
28:861:73356:21:20:90:525:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:fraction  of  papers  in  the  list  make  use  of  data  from Europe  (85 papers), while  smaller 
28:862:73454:20:21:90:525:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:shares  makes  use  of  data  from South  America  (18  papers), Africa  (6  papers), Asia  (4 
28:863:73548:21:21:90:525:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:papers), and  Oceania  (1  paper).  Within  Europe the majority  of  papers  come  from 
28:864:73635:21:20:90:525:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:England, Israel, Norway,  and  Sweden.  These four countries  comprise 77%  of European 
28:865:73720:20:21:90:525:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:output.  Within  United  States,  the majority  of  research  comes  from  North  Carolina, 
28:866:73811:21:21:90:525:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Florida,  Texas,  Chicago, and  New  York  City; however,  nearly  half  of  the  States  in  the 
28:867:73907:21:22:90:524:108:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Union  contributed  at least  one  paper  to  the  list,  and  given  the  large  investments  in  data 
28:868:74011:22:8:234:237:86:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:!:                                                        
28:869:74066:30:0:90:347:78:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:13 We treat Israel as part of Europe for our accounting purposes. 
29:870:74132:0:21:90:525:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:infrastructure  throughout  the  United  States  we  expect  the  geographic  spread  to  continue 
29:871:74231:21:21:90:525:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:in the future. That said, it is not an accident that so many papers make use of data from 
29:872:74321:21:20:90:524:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:North  Carolina,  Florida,  Texas,  Chicago,  and  New  York  City,  as  these  are  major  U.S. 
29:873:74418:20:21:90:525:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:jurisdictions  that  facilitate  research  more  than  most.  Among  other  countries  Chile 
29:874:74511:21:21:90:524:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:contributed  11  papers, while Canada 9.  There  is  also  growing  output  based  on  Kenyan 
29:875:74603:21:21:90:524:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:data. It is also clear from tables 1 to 4 that majority of the research output utilizes only a 
29:876:74697:21:20:90:525:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:single  administrative  data  source  (e.g.  school  records)  which  could  be  related  to  both 
29:877:74796:20:21:90:525:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:limited data infrastructure and matching restrictions (e.g. in the US). At the same time it 
29:878:74886:21:21:90:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:is   relatively   rare   that   researchers   are   able   to   match   individuals   across   multiple 
29:879:74990:21:20:90:525:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:administrative data sets, say birth and school records, and also to survey or experiment – 
29:880:75080:20:21:90:464:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:only 10 out of 350 paper we identified and primarily from outside of the US.  
29:881:75157:21:21:126:525:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:As  stated  in  the  introduction,  the  use  of  administrative  data  is  a  rather  new 
29:882:75248:21:21:90:525:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:phenomenon and it has  been made possible due  to the increase in computational power, 
29:883:75335:21:20:90:525:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:decrease in storage prices and enhanced cooperation between governmental agencies and 
29:884:75421:20:21:90:525:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:researchers all over the world. The first papers from our list were published in Economics 
29:885:75512:21:21:90:524:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of Education Review (Theobald, 1990) and in the Journal of Human Resources (Murnane 
29:886:75594:21:20:90:524:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and Olsen, 1990). The former one used data from Washington, while the latter one from 
29:887:75679:20:21:90:524:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:North  Carolina,  and  both  papers  investigated  the  role  that  different  variables  play  in 
29:888:75778:21:21:90:525:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:teacher  retention.  In  fact  through  the  1990s  the  surveyed  journals  published  only  seven 
29:889:75878:21:20:90:524:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:papers using administrative data and six of these were studying the teacher labor market. 
29:890:75967:20:21:90:525:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:One reason for the focus on teachers in the early use of administrative data is the fact that 
29:891:76061:21:21:90:525:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:due to bureaucracy and budgeting the records of public school employees were compiled 
29:892:76147:21:21:90:525:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and stored centrally by state departments of education long before researchers expressed 
29:893:76236:21:20:90:524:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:interest  in  them,  while  few  countries  around  the  world  systematically  collected  student 
29:894:76335:20:21:90:216:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:achievement information. 
29:895:76359:21:21:126:525:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:In  the  2000s  there  was  a  rapid  increase  in  the  amount  of  scientific  output  using 
29:896:76454:21:20:90:524:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:administrative data with 114 papers published in our list. The diversity also increased and 
29:897:76545:20:21:90:525:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:papers used not only data on teachers and students but also on individuals pre- and post- 
29:898:76632:21:21:90:525:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:their  schooling  years.  Finally,  between  2010  and  July  2014  the  scientific  journals  we 
29:899:76730:21:21:90:524:108:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:surveyed have already  published  nearly  230  papers.  This  massive  increase  was  driven 
29:900:76823:21:0:90:525:87:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:mostly by the United States, but in every year more and more countries contribute to the 
30:901:76913:0:21:90:525:709:12:g_d0_f3:12:Times New Roman:B:global “data village”. The first papers in  our  list using  European  data  were  published  in 
30:902:77010:21:21:90:524:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:2001 using  data from  Jerusalem,  from  South  America  in  2000  using  Chilean  data, from 
30:903:77102:21:20:90:489:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Asia in 2009 using data from Beijing, and from Africa in 2009 using Kenyan data. 
30:904:77181:20:21:126:525:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Akin to the examples provided in our Norway, Sweden, and Florida case studies, 
30:905:77260:21:21:90:524:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:we observe a substantial variation in the types of registry data used internationally. This 
30:906:77352:21:21:90:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:depends  both  on  data  infrastructure  itself  but  also  on  the  institutional  setting  in  a 
30:907:77451:21:20:90:525:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:particular country, state or region under investigation. For example, even though Norway 
30:908:77540:20:21:90:524:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:has  very  high-quality long  run  data  it  is difficult to  study  the  long-run  effects  of  school 
30:909:77642:21:21:90:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:competition in this country because there is no variation in the competitive pressure faced 
30:910:77733:21:20:90:524:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:by different schools. Similarly, although Sweden has introduced school competition to its 
30:911:77823:20:21:90:525:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:institutional  setting  and  hence  it  is  possible  to  study  whether  such  policies  have  long 
30:912:77924:21:21:90:525:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:lasting  effects,  it  is  actually  impossible  to  look  at  these  effects  in  a  short-run,  i.e., in  a 
30:913:78033:21:21:90:525:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:manner  comparable  to  the  United States,  because  Sweden  did  not  test  its  pupils  using 
30:914:78130:21:20:90:525:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:standardized  assessments.  Yet  another  problem  is  the  possibility  to  link  different  data 
30:915:78229:20:21:90:525:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:registers, and from this perspective in most states in the United States it is not possible to 
30:916:78323:21:21:90:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:study  the  effects  of,  for  example,  neonatal  health  on  schooling  outcomes (Table  2).  The 
30:917:78422:21:20:90:525:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:data simply do not allow a clean match between  birth records and school records due to 
30:918:78510:20:21:90:524:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:lack  of  unique personal  identifier.  Notable  exception  here  is  Florida  that  assigns  their 
30:919:78610:21:21:90:524:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:newborns social security numbers. Useful but not perfect way around this last problem is 
30:920:78698:21:20:90:525:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:widely used in historical research probabilistic matching of individuals (Ferrie and Long, 
30:921:78789:20:21:90:525:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:2013).  This  method  has  been  applied  to  some  modern  data  sets  like  birth  and  school 
30:922:78886:21:21:90:524:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:records  in  North  Carolina  (Ladd  et  al.,  2012) but  the  match  rates  based  on  these 
30:923:78980:21:21:90:518:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:procedures are not ideal and they are sensitive to the type of populations under scrutiny.  
30:924:79070:21:20:126:525:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:The  examples  in  the  paragraph  above  illustrate  the  complexity  behind  research 
30:925:79158:20:21:90:525:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:projects involving  registry  data but also point out to the need of both data infrastructure 
30:926:79251:21:21:90:524:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and  credible  variation  in  studying  economic and  educational phenomena.  The  agenda 
30:927:79341:21:20:90:525:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:becomes  even  more  complex  when  the  research  objectives  involve  long-run  effects  of 
30:928:79435:20:21:90:525:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:particular interventions, their spillovers or understanding the mechanisms through which 
30:929:79524:21:21:90:525:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:these  interventions  operate.  In  this  case  population-level  administrative  registries  are 
30:930:79622:21:21:90:525:108:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:particularly  essential as  these  research  projects  often  involve  matching  subjects  in  field 
30:931:79722:21:0:90:525:87:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:experiments to themselves decades later (Aslund, et al., 2011) or to subjects’ siblings 
31:932:79812:0:21:90:525:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:(Black  et  al.,  2014).  Furthermore,  when  the  goal  is  to  elicit  mechanisms  through  which 
31:933:79912:21:21:90:524:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the  policies  operate  then  most  often  the  survey  instruments  need  to  be  applied to  the 
31:934:80011:21:20:90:525:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:studied  populations  and  then  matched  back  to  the  original  registers  (Burgess  et  al., 
31:935:80108:20:21:90:159:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:forthcoming). 
31:936:80121:21:21:126:525:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Due  to  the  institutional  issues  brought  up  in  the  paragraphs  above  researchers  in 
31:937:80215:21:21:90:524:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:different  countries  seem  to  specialize  in  studying  very  specific  questions  based  on  the 
31:938:80315:21:20:90:524:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:registers   that   are   available   to   them,   and   the   policy   environments   that   they   face. 
31:939:80421:20:21:90:525:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Scandinavian   countries   produce   mostly   studies   that   involve   rather   lower   quality 
31:940:80519:21:21:90:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:educational  measures  for  which  they  compensate  with  the  fact  that  individuals  can  be 
31:941:80616:21:20:90:525:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:tracked from their birth to their death and often also across generations14. These countries 
31:942:80709:20:21:90:525:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:do  not  have  longitudinal  student  assessment  data  but  are  the  only  locations  in  the  world 
31:943:80812:21:21:90:525:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:where  the  whole  population  of  males  undergoes  physical,  intellectual  and  emotional 
31:944:80905:21:21:90:524:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:evaluations  at  the  time  of  entering  adulthood15.  On  the  other  side  of  this  spectrum  are 
31:945:81007:21:20:90:524:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:countries  like  England  or the majority  of the U.S. states  that  have  regular  student 
31:946:81099:20:21:90:525:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:assessments  but  do  not  allow  merging  different  databases.  A  few  notable  exceptions  to 
31:947:81197:21:21:90:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:that   rule   are   for   instance   Florida, Texas,   Chicago,   Charlotte-Mecklenburg (North 
31:948:81291:21:20:90:522:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Carolina), and  New  York  City  that  allow  linking  student  records  to  subsequent  post-
31:949:81385:20:21:90:524:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:secondary  education  (Booker  et  al.,  2011),  criminal  records  (Deming,  2011)  or  labor 
31:950:81480:21:21:90:525:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:market  outcomes  (Clark  and  Martorell,  2014).  These  are  generally  rare  because  they 
31:951:81574:21:20:90:524:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:require agreements and cooperation of multiple governmental agencies16. A longitudinal 
31:952:81661:20:21:90:524:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:data set that follows kids from birth through childhood, adolescence to adulthood is also 
31:953:81750:21:21:90:525:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:available  for  the  province  of  Manitoba,  Canada.  These  data  are  somewhat  in-between 
31:954:81844:21:21:90:524:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Scandinavian   and   United States registers   because   although   they   allow   tracking 
31:955:81935:21:20:90:525:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:individuals  longitudinally,  they  do  not  allow  for  more  complex  familial  linkages or 
31:956:82028:20:34:90:524:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:longitudinal   student   assessment.   There   are   also   few data   sets   with   longitudinal 
31:957:82126:34:8:234:237:178:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:!:                                                        
31:958:82181:42:16:90:512:170:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:14 A notable exception here is Finland where research community has not have until recently such a wide 
31:959:82283:16:7:90:344:154:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:access to national registers as in Denmark, Sweden or Norway. 
31:960:82344:7:16:90:513:147:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:15 The mandatory military draft has been revoked in Sweden in the mid 2000s but the data for the cohorts 
31:961:82447:16:11:90:524:131:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:1952 to 2002 can still be used. At the same time as discussed in our case studies Sweden is in the process of 
31:962:82554:11:7:90:503:120:10:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:*:rolling out longitudinal student assessments in their compulsory schooling system in grades 3, 6 and 9. 
31:963:82656:7:16:90:522:113:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:16 Note that in Scandinavia, unlike in the US, the multiple registers are handled by a single agency and even 
31:964:82764:16:12:90:518:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:though Department of Defense administers the military draft and Department of Education coordinates the 
31:965:82868:12:11:90:507:85:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:9th grade assessments the research proposal is submitted and processed through a single Data Inspection 
31:966:82971:11:0:90:133:74:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:Authority. 
32:967:82983:0:21:90:525:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:components outside of Scandinavia or North America. For instance, it is possible to link 
32:968:83072:21:21:90:524:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:birth  records  to  schooling  records  in  Chile  (Bharadwaj,  Loken  and  Neilson,  2013),  link 
32:969:83171:21:20:90:525:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:birth  records  to  death  records  to  schooling  records  in  Taiwan  (Gimenez  et  al.,  2013)  or 
32:970:83273:20:21:90:443:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:link schooling interventions to long-run outcomes in Israel (Lavy, 2014). 
32:971:83346:21:21:126:525:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:The  growth  in  access  to  administrative  data  across  the  World  is  crucial  from  the 
32:972:83440:21:21:90:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:policy  point  of  view  because  it  allows  direct  testing  of  external  validity  of  particular 
32:973:83542:21:20:90:525:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:economic  phenomena  in  different  institutional  setting.  In  fact  we  see  more  and  more 
32:974:83638:20:21:90:525:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:multi-state  or  multi-country  studies  in  recent  years, e.g.  Fryer  (2014)  or  Bharadwaj, 
32:975:83733:21:21:90:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Loken and  Neilson  (2013)17.  The  concern with  external  validity  and  ability  to  study  the 
32:976:83831:21:20:90:525:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:same  policies  in  multiple  locations  is  the  more  important  in  experimental  work  that 
32:977:83927:20:21:90:525:502:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:necessarily focuses on rather narrow populations, but is becoming a “gold standard” in 
32:978:84014:21:21:90:524:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:policy  evaluations.  The  single-country  multi-site  studies  are  important  from  national 
32:979:84109:21:21:90:525:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:policy point of view, especially in diverse countries like United States or France, because 
32:980:84201:21:20:90:525:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:it  is  not  obvious  that  intervention  which  works  in  Chicago  Public  Schools  or  East Paris 
32:981:84302:20:21:90:525:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:will  work  in  more  affluent  areas  like  Greenwich,  Connecticut  or  Neuilly-sur-Seine. 
32:982:84395:21:21:90:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Another  broader  question  is  whether  similar  policies  give  the  same  effects  in  culturally, 
32:983:84497:21:20:90:524:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:economically or institutionally different environment. In this case researchers have to rely 
32:984:84590:20:21:90:525:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:on   rare   interventions   that   are   universal   across   many   countries,   like   for   example 
32:985:84693:21:21:90:525:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:standardized  treatment  of  low  birth  weight  babies. These  studies  are  extremely  valuable 
32:986:84790:21:20:90:524:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:because   they   often   allow   research   community   to   understand   a   more   fundamental 
32:987:84887:20:21:90:525:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:background of human social behavior. They also allow studying externalities of particular 
32:988:84977:21:21:90:387:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:policies interacting with different institutional environments.  
32:989:85041:21:21:126:525:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:In  the  remaining  part  of  this  section  we  focus  on  particular  questions  relevant  to 
32:990:85137:21:20:90:524:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:educational research agenda, and how these have been addressed in different countries or 
32:991:85226:20:21:90:525:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:states.  We  start  off  with  the  fundamental  question  of  how  early  childhood  environment 
32:992:85324:21:21:90:524:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:affects   educational,   and   potentially   long-run   outcomes.   Given   the   advantages   and 
32:993:85423:21:20:90:524:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:disadvantages of various administrative data sets described in the paragraphs above, it is 
32:994:85514:20:30:90:525:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:not  surprising  that  this  research  question  has  been  dominated  by  studies  based  on 
32:995:85608:30:7:234:237:120:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:!:                                                        
32:996:85663:37:16:90:515:113:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:17 There is fewer published cross-country than cross-state studies, however, we should see more and more 
32:997:85767:16:12:90:512:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:of the former ones coming in the next few years. Another notable example is study of Bedard and Dhuey 
32:998:85869:12:11:90:512:85:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:(2006) which combines results from Canada based on administrative data and from other countries based 
32:999:85971:11:0:90:184:74:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:on various survey data. 
33:1000:85996:0:21:90:524:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Scandinavian  data (Table  2).  The  excellent  data  infrastructure  in  Denmark,  Sweden  and 
33:1001:86091:21:21:90:525:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Norway allows tracking individuals not only from their birth to their death but also across 
33:1002:86183:21:20:90:525:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:multiple  generations  and  familial  connections  as  children  are  linked  to  their  biological 
33:1003:86283:20:21:90:524:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:parents using unique identifiers, and the parents are in turn linked to their siblings using 
33:1004:86376:21:21:90:525:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:unique  identifiers.  Except  for  the  three  aforementioned  Scandinavian  countries  early 
33:1005:86470:21:21:90:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:childhood  has  also  been  studied  in  two  other  European  countries:  England  (Almond, 
33:1006:86563:21:20:90:525:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Mazumder  and  Van  Ewijk,  2014)  and  Germany  (Dustmann  and  Schonberg,  2012).  In 
33:1007:86651:20:21:90:524:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:North America we have a birth order study from Indiana (Hanushek, 1992) which is the 
33:1008:86736:21:21:90:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:only  study  from  the  1990s  on  our  list  that  was  not  focused  specifically  on  teachers  but 
33:1009:86839:21:20:90:525:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:used an experimental population from Gary  Income Maintenance Experiment merged to 
33:1010:86922:20:21:90:525:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:children schooling records. The other papers include birth weight effects  estimates from 
33:1011:87012:21:21:90:524:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Canada  (Oreopoulos  et  al.,  2008)  and  Florida  (Figlio  et  al.,  2014),  in-utero  pollution 
33:1012:87111:21:21:90:525:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:exposure  study  from  Texas  (Sanders,  2012)  and  an  influential  foster  care  system

33:1014:87302:20:21:90:524:419:12:g_d0_f3:12:Times New Roman:B:parental loss on children’s well-being  (Gimenez  et  al.,  2013)  while  a  paper  based  on 
33:1015:87396:21:21:90:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Chilean and Norwegian data studies the role of health interventions at birth (Bharadwaj, 
33:1016:87485:21:20:90:524:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Loken and Neilson, 2013). Some of these papers, due to their use of administrative data, 
33:1017:87573:20:21:90:524:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:documented new and important empirical phenomena. Figlio et al. (2014) are among the 
33:1018:87658:21:21:90:525:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:first  to  document  that  neonatal  health  and  parental  socioeconomic  status  are  likely 
33:1019:87753:21:20:90:524:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:complements  rather  than  substitutes – a  common  perception  was  rather  that  wealthier 
33:1020:87845:20:21:90:525:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:parents  can  better  compensate  for  lower  health  capital  of  their  children  than  poorer 
33:1021:87942:21:21:90:525:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:parents.  Bharadwaj,  Lokean  and  Neilson  (2013)  show  that  health  interventions  in 
33:1022:88032:21:21:90:524:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:countries  as  different  as  Chile  and  Norway  can  yield  fairly  similar  effects  which  boosts 
33:1023:88134:21:20:90:525:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the confidence that earl life interventions effectiveness is not necessarily tied to specific 
33:1024:88228:20:21:90:332:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:institutional environment or wealth of the society. 
33:1025:88279:21:21:126:525:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Across   different   countries   and   institutional   settings   the   most   often   studied 
33:1026:88374:21:20:90:525:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:question seems to be the role of school technology or the education production function. 
33:1027:88462:20:21:90:525:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:These  topics  range  from  the  questions  of  how  gender  composition  of  classrooms 
33:1028:88551:21:21:90:524:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:influences  female  school  choice  in  Austria  (Schneeweis  and  Zweimuller,  2012),  or  how 
33:1029:88647:21:0:90:525:108:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:ethnic and immigrant concentration in schools affects cognitive development of children
