34:1031:88821:21:21:90:525:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Schonberg,   2010), through   mandatory   school   entry   and   exit   ages   in   Germany 
34:1032:88912:21:20:90:525:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:(Muhlenweg  and  Puhani,  2010)  and  the  Netherlands  (Cabus  and  De  Witte,  2011)  to 
34:1033:89003:20:21:90:525:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:school  resources  in  Norway  (Haegeland,  Raaum  and  Salvanes,  2012),  Canada  (Leach, 
34:1034:89094:21:21:90:525:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Payne  and  Chan,  2010)  and  New  York  City  (Rubenstein  et  al.,  2009). There  is  also  a 
34:1035:89190:21:21:90:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:substantial  variation  in  the  kind  of  inputs  that  are  investigated  in  different  states  within 
34:1036:89296:21:20:90:525:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the  Union.  They  span  from  the  role  of  the  quantity  of  math  instruction  hours  in  Florida 
34:1037:89399:20:21:90:525:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:(Taylor, 2014) through teacher cheating in Chicago (Jacob and Levitt, 2003) to the role of 
34:1038:89490:21:21:90:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:school  crowding  in  North  Carolina  (McMullen  and  Rouse,  2012)  or  paying  students  for 
34:1039:89586:21:20:90:307:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:grade completion in Ohio (Bettinger, 2012).  
34:1040:89630:20:21:126:524:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:There  are  also  multi-site  studies  within  the  US  that  explore  the  role  of  same 
34:1041:89721:21:21:90:525:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:school  inputs  in very  different  school  environments,  and  thus,  allow  for  assessment  of 
34:1042:89818:21:21:90:525:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:generalizability of the interventions. An example of such study  would be Fryer’s (2014) 
34:1043:89906:21:20:90:525:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:investigation  of the  role  of  importing  best  charter  school  practices  to  traditional  public 
34:1044:90007:20:21:90:525:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:schools  in  Chicago,  Denver  and  Houston.  His  results  are  remarkably  similar  across 
34:1045:90100:21:21:90:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Denver and Houston, the two experimental samples, and are smaller for Chicago, where 
34:1046:90185:21:20:90:525:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:only  quasi-experimental  variation  is  available.  Notably  Denver  and  Houston  differ  both 
34:1047:90282:20:21:90:525:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:in  terms  of  demographics  and  institutional  setting  so  the  similarity  of  the  estimates  is 
34:1048:90384:21:21:90:525:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:noteworthy. It is also the case that Chicago implemented a slightly less intensive program 
34:1049:90475:21:20:90:525:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:which  could  account  for  the  difference  in  the  effects.  Another  example  of  this  kind  of 
34:1050:90576:20:21:90:524:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:cross-sites  within-country  research  is  Abdulkadiroglu,  Angrist  and  Pathak  (2014)  who 
34:1051:90670:21:21:90:525:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:investigate  the  role  of  school  composition  on  student  achievement  in  Boston  and  New 
34:1052:90766:21:21:90:524:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:York. In both cities they find little evidence that attending elite schools has a causal effect 
34:1053:90862:21:20:90:525:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:on test scores or college quality. Similar findings are confirmed in Kenyan setting (Lucas 
34:1054:90953:20:21:90:525:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and  Mbiti,  2014)  but  Jackson  (2010)  finds  large  gains  from  attending  elite  schools  in 
34:1055:91052:21:48:90:524:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Trinidad and Tobago. This set of papers unlike the health interventions at birth suggests 
34:1056:91142:48:7:234:237:143:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:!:                                                        
34:1057:91197:55:16:90:493:136:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:18 The Danish study is the more important because it merges PISA data with registry data which in a 
34:1058:91296:16:12:90:510:120:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:longer-run will allow benchmarking the PISA test scores against economically meaningful variables like 
34:1059:91398:12:11:90:500:108:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:university graduation or income. Since PISA is used globally to compare the efficiency of educational 
34:1060:91500:11:12:90:496:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:systems it seems imperative to understand how PISA scores translate into long-run outcomes. To our 
34:1061:91599:12:11:90:504:85:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:knowledge Denmark is the only country that successfully merged their PISA samples to administrative 
34:1062:91699:11:0:90:126:74:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:records.  
35:1063:91710:0:21:90:525:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:that  some  educational  policies  might  be  generalizable  with  country  but  not  across 
35:1064:91803:21:21:90:143:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:countires.  
35:1065:91813:21:20:126:525:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:One  particular  school  attribute  that  gained  a  lot  of  attention  in  the  educational 
35:1066:91907:20:21:90:524:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:research agenda involves class size (Angrist and Lavy, 1999; Chetty et al. 2011). Neither 
35:1067:91997:21:21:90:525:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of these two papers used administrative educational data sets, but there exists evidence on 
35:1068:92087:21:21:90:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:this  topic from at  least four  countries  and  two  states  using educational administrative 
35:1069:92181:21:20:90:525:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:data.  This  question  has  been  studied  in  Denmark  (Heinesen,  2010),  Italy  (Angrist, 
35:1070:92274:20:21:90:525:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Battisin and Vuri, 2014), Sweden (Fredriksson, Ockert and Oosterbeek, 2013), and in the 
35:1071:92362:21:21:90:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:United States in  Florida  (Chingos,  2012).  Using different  identification  strategies  and 
35:1072:92456:21:20:90:525:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:data  these  papers  generally  find  conflating  results.  Danish,  Italian  and  Swedish  studies 
35:1073:92556:20:21:90:525:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:confirm the previous results based on survey data that smaller classes generate significant 
35:1074:92648:21:21:90:525:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:advantages in later life schooling and labor market outcomes. On the contrary the Florida 
35:1075:92738:21:21:90:524:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:case-study  and  also  another  paper  using  Norwegian  registry  data  (Leuven,  Oosterbeek 
35:1076:92832:21:20:90:525:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and  Ronning,  2008)  do  not  find  much  of  an  effect  of  a  reduction  in  class  size.  It  is 
35:1077:92934:20:21:90:524:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:particularly   interesting   that   the   Swedish   and   Norwegian   studies   use an identical 
35:1078:93031:21:21:90:524:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:identification strategy but find very different results. This point makes clear the value of 
35:1079:93124:21:20:90:271:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:cross-context replication and studies. 
35:1080:93162:20:21:126:525:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:The  two  remaining  studies  of  class  size  in  our  list  are  somewhat  different. 
35:1081:93249:21:21:90:525:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Complementary  research  from  Kentucky  (Barrett  and  Toma,  2013)  documents  that 
35:1082:93335:21:20:90:525:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:principals  are  more  likely  to  assign  more  effective  teachers  to  larger  classes,  potentially 
35:1083:93439:20:21:90:525:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:to  compensate  for  the  negative  class-size  effects.  Finally,  a  Chilean  (Urquiola  and 
35:1084:93534:21:21:90:524:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Verhoogen,   2009)   paper   makes   a   more   methodological   point   by   documenting   an 
35:1085:93629:21:21:90:525:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:inverted-U cross-sectional relationship between class-size and household income as well 
35:1086:93717:21:20:90:525:232:12:g_d0_f3:12:Times New Roman:B:as stacking of schools’ enrollments at multiples of the class-size cap. These two data facts 
35:1087:93810:20:21:90:525:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:could  invalidate  non-experimental  or regression  discontinuity estimates  of  the  class-size 
35:1088:93906:21:21:90:525:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:in  liberalized  market  settings  where  schools  are  free  to  set  prices  and/or  turn  away 
35:1089:94004:21:20:90:522:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:students,  and  households  are  free  to  sort  between  schools.  The  manipulation  of a class-
35:1090:94102:20:21:90:525:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:size  rule  that  can  potentially  invalidate  the regression  discontinuity estimates  has  also 
35:1091:94200:21:21:90:524:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:been  documented  in  Israel  (Cohen-Zada,  Gradstein  and  Reuven,  2013). Comprehensive 
35:1092:94289:21:0:90:507:108:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:administrative data facilitated these studies that otherwise would be harder to conduct. 
36:1093:94379:0:21:126:525:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Another  hotly  debated  in  the  past  decades  educational  policy  topic  has  been  the 
36:1094:94471:21:21:90:525:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:role  of  school  choice  and  competition. Around  the  world, governments have  recently 
36:1095:94560:21:20:90:525:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:implemented and researchers evaluated various forms of choice and competition. Outside 
36:1096:94647:20:21:90:524:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:the United States the countries that contributed to this broad research agenda are England, 
36:1097:94738:21:21:90:524:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Israel, and Sweden in Europe, Canada and United States in North America, Colombia and 
36:1098:94821:21:21:90:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Chile in South America, and China in Asia. However, not all of these countries study the 
36:1099:94910:21:20:90:524:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:same  phenomena  that  we  encapsulate  in  a  single  broad term of  school  choice.  For 
36:1100:95000:20:21:90:525:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:example, outside the United States, the effects of voucher and charter schools on student 
36:1101:95089:21:21:90:524:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:outcomes  are  examined  in  England  (Clark,  2009),  Sweden  (Sandstrom  and  Bergstrom, 
36:1102:95180:21:20:90:525:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:2005),  Chile  (Mizala  and  Romaguera,  2000)  and  Colombia  (Angrist,  Bettinger  and

36:1104:95355:21:21:90:525:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of early Chilean descriptive work, point towards beneficial effects of vouchers on student 
36:1105:95445:21:21:90:525:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:achievement.  An  interesting  modification  of  the  voucher  system  type  of  competition  is 
36:1106:95542:21:20:90:524:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:studied  in  Ontario,  Canada (Card,  Dooley  and  Payne,  2010)  where  non-Catholics  are 
36:1107:95633:20:21:90:525:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:subject to monopoly of public schools while Catholics (40% of children in the province) 
36:1108:95721:21:21:90:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:can  choose  between  sending  their  kids  to  secular  public  schools  or  to  separate  schools. 
36:1109:95822:21:20:90:470:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:The authors also find test score gains due to increased competition in Ontario.  
36:1110:95902:20:21:126:525:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:These effects have  also been investigated in the  United States for Florida (Figlio 
36:1111:95986:21:21:90:525:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and  Hart,  2014),  Chicago  (Booker  et  al.,  2011),  Massachusetts  (Angrist,  Pathak  and 
36:1112:96080:21:20:90:524:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Walters,  2013),  New  York  City  (Winters,  2012),  Texas  (Booker  et  al.,  2007)  and  Utah 
36:1113:96177:20:21:90:525:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:(Ni  and  Rorrer,  2012).  The  results  generally  suggest  heterogeneous  effects  of  charters 
36:1114:96275:21:21:90:525:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:which might be either due to the fact that they apply different identification strategies or

37:1128:97591:21:21:90:240:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:for differing research findings. 
37:1129:97623:21:21:126:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Another  strand  of  this  agenda  considers  the  role  of  parents  in  school  choice  in

37:1135:98176:21:21:90:525:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:2005). Finally, competition and school choice may affect not only students but also their 
37:1136:98266:21:21:90:524:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:teachers, and we discuss this research agenda below where we focus more broadly on the

37:1146:99112:21:21:90:525:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:widely  studied  question  is  likely  the  teacher  labor  supply  and  mobility  that  has  been

37:1148:99300:20:21:90:525:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and Stinebrickner, 2007), Kentucky (Cowen et al., 2012), Michigan (Gershenson, 2012), 
37:1149:99386:21:21:90:525:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Missouri (Podgursky, Monroe and Watson, 2004), North Carolina (Jackson, 2013), New 
37:1150:99469:21:20:90:525:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:York (Brewer, 1996), Texas (Hanushek, Kain and Rivkin, 2004), Washington (Theobald, 
37:1151:99553:20:21:90:524:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:1990),  Wisconsin  (Imezeki,  2005);  and  internationally  in  Italy  (Barbieri,  Rossetti and 
37:1152:99648:21:0:90:525:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Sestito,  2011),  Norway  (Falch  and  Strom,  2005),  Sweden  (Karbownik,  2014)  and 
38:1153:99737:0:21:90:524:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Venezuela  (Ortega,  2010)19. The  broad  conclusion  from  these  papers  is  that  school 
38:1154:99828:21:21:90:525:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:quality  and  working  conditions  matter  for  attracting  and  retaining  teachers,  particularly 
38:1155:99928:21:20:90:524:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:those  of  higher  quality,  but  particular  factors  differ  across  sites  in  both  whether  they 
38:1156:100030:20:21:90:257:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:matter and how much they matter. 
38:1157:100062:21:21:126:524:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:Another related topic that is present only in the United States research, to the best 
38:1158:100147:21:21:90:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of  our  knowledge, is  the  role  of  teacher  retirement and  the  retirement  benefits.  This 
38:1159:100242:21:20:90:525:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:particular  question  has  been  studied  in  Arkansas  (Costrell  and  McGee,  2010),  Illinois 
38:1160:100339:20:21:90:525:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:(Fitzpatrick   and   Lovenheim,   2014),   Missouri   (Koedel,   Ni   and   Podgursky,   2014), 
38:1161:100435:21:21:90:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Pennsylvania  (Ferguson,  Strauss  and  Vogt,  2006)  and  Washington  (DeArmond  and 
38:1162:100521:21:20:90:525:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Goldhaber,  2010).  Some  other  studies  consider  the  role  of  incentives  in  improving 
38:1163:100614:20:21:90:525:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:teacher  performance  in  Denver  (Goldhaber  and  Walch,  2012),  Chicago  (Jacob,  2013), 
38:1164:100706:21:21:90:524:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Kentucky  (Barrett and Toma, 2013),  New York  City (Fryer, 2013), Houston (Imberman 
38:1165:100791:21:21:90:422:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and Lovenheim, 2015) and outside of the US in Israel (Lavy, 2009).  
38:1166:100857:21:20:126:524:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:A  lot  of  attention  in  the  United States has  also  been  given  to  the  interaction 
38:1167:100947:20:21:90:525:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:between  the  schools,  teachers  and  their  students.  School  accountability  was  introduced 
38:1168:101044:21:21:90:525:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:voluntarily by many states in the 1990s but with the introduction of the federal No Child 
38:1169:101133:21:20:90:525:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Left Behind law in 2002 the remaining states were required to start measuring the relative 
38:1170:101222:20:21:90:525:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:performance  of  their  students,  which  by  extension  allowed  calculations  of  value  added 
38:1171:101319:21:21:90:525:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:measures, assessment of teacher effectiveness and as an unintended side-effect produced 
38:1172:101406:21:20:90:524:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:large  quantities  of  administrative  data  on  teacher  and  their  students (Figlio  and  Loeb, 
38:1173:101505:20:21:90:525:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:2011).  Based  on  our  selection  of  journals  we  found  value  added  or  accountability 
38:1174:101598:21:21:90:525:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:research from San Diego (Koedel and Betts, 2010), Colorado (Briggs and Weeks, 2009), 
38:1175:101683:21:21:90:524:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Florida  (Sass,  Semykina  and  Harris,  2014),  Chicago  (Aaronson,  Barrow  and  Sander, 
38:1176:101774:21:20:90:525:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:2007), North Carolina (Rothstein, 2010), Texas (Rivkin, Hanushek and Kain, 2005), and 
38:1177:101860:20:21:90:525:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Washington  (Krieg,  2011).  Outside  of  the  United States,  value  added  models  have  also 
38:1178:101956:21:21:90:524:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:been   examined   in   two   other   English   speaking   countries,   mainly   England   (Ray, 
38:1179:102052:21:20:90:379:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:McCormack and Evans, 2009) and Australia (Leigh, 2010). 
38:1180:102107:20:21:126:525:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:There  are  many  other  research  themes  that  we  did  not  cover  in  this  brief  review 
38:1181:102201:21:32:90:524:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and which gained considerable attention in the research community. To name a few from 
38:1182:102286:32:7:234:237:97:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:!:                                                        
38:1183:102341:39:16:90:514:90:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:19 Many of these states and countries contributed multiple studies on the topic of teacher labor supply and 
38:1184:102448:16:0:90:130:74:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:D:mobility.  
39:1185:102460:0:21:90:525:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:our extensive but incomplete list, registry data have been used to study: the introduction 
39:1186:102551:21:21:90:525:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of   new   technologies   to   schools   in   England   (Machin,   McNally   and   Silva,   2007), 
39:1187:102650:21:20:90:525:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:Times New Roman:B:experimental  evidence  on  schools  influence  on  parents’  involvement  in  education  in 
39:1188:102742:20:21:90:525:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:France   (Avvisati   et   al.,   2014),   experimental   evidence   on   gender   differences   in 
39:1189:102841:21:21:90:524:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:competitiveness and its consequences for educational choices in the Netherlands (Buser, 
39:1190:102928:21:21:90:524:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Niederle  and  Oosterbeek,  2014),  the  role  of  school  quality  in  Romania  (Pop-Elches  and 
39:1191:103026:21:20:90:524:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:Urquiola,  2013),  experimental  evidence  on  learning  incentives  in  Mexico  (Behrman  et 
39:1192:103120:20:21:90:524:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:al., 2015),  perceived  effects  of  school  quality  on  housing  market  (Figlio  and  Lucas, 
39:1193:103216:21:21:90:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:2004),  the  role  of  peer  effects  utilizing  student  reshuffling  due  to  extreme  events 
39:1194:103312:21:20:90:524:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:(Imberman, Kugler and Sacerdote, 2012) or the ability of principals to recognize effective 
39:1195:103403:20:21:90:525:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:teachers   (Jacob   and   Lefgren,   2008).   We   also   have   not   mentioned   some   unique 
39:1196:103500:21:21:90:525:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:educational  data  sets  used  worldwide  to  address  very  specific  research  questions.  These 
39:1197:103599:21:21:90:525:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:would be GED takers in Florida and Texas (Tyler, Murnane and Willett, 2004), principals 
39:1198:103687:21:20:90:525:439:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:in Illinois and North Carolina (Gates et al., 2006), college entry exam takers in Michigan 
39:1199:103777:20:21:90:525:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:(Andrews,  DesJardins  and  Ranchhod,  2010)  or anthropometric  measurements of  school 
39:1200:103865:21:21:90:237:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:children in Peru (Dell, 2010).  
39:1201:103896:21:20:126:524:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A:In  summary, there  is  a  growing  prevalence  in  the  use  of  administrative  data  in 
39:1202:103987:20:21:90:525:357:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:educational research and in this section we hoped to provide some brief overview of this 
39:1203:104076:21:21:90:524:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:phenomenon internationally. We did not and could not aim to be complete here, however, 
39:1204:104163:21:20:90:525:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:our  goal  was  to  provide  useful  examples  of  applications  and  data  types  utilized  in 
39:1205:104259:20:21:90:524:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:different countries. It is clear that there are many opportunities to study new questions in 
39:1206:104351:21:21:90:525:274:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:new environments, and  we expect that the explosion in the use of administrative data in 
39:1207:104440:21:21:90:362:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:education research will only continue to expand rapidly. 
39:1208:104496:21:21:126:129:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:!: 
39:1209:104496:42:20:90:174:211:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:C:VI. Conclusions 
39:1210:104511:20:21:126:525:191:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:A: It  is  evident  that  administrative  data  present  a  world  of  opportunity,  and  while 
39:1211:104604:21:20:90:525:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:there are clearly challenges associated with the use of administrative data, the benefits of 
39:1212:104697:20:21:90:525:150:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:collecting these data and using them for research and policy purposes surely outweigh the 
39:1213:104787:21:21:90:525:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:costs  involved.  While  administrative  data  are  not  a  substitute  for  many  purpose-built 
39:1214:104884:21:21:90:524:108:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:survey  data,  in  the  cases  in  which  they  are  substitutes  they  have  the  potential  to  save 
39:1215:104987:21:0:90:525:87:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:taxpayers  considerable  amounts  of  money  while  delivering  better-quality  data,  and  of 
40:1216:105084:0:21:90:525:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:course  there  are  many  ways  in  which  administrative  data  can  make  survey  data  better, 
40:1217:105182:21:21:90:524:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:more  cost-effective,  and  more  flexible. The  availability  of  these  data  has  led  to  new 
40:1218:105280:21:20:90:525:667:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:research   questions   that   had   previously   not   been   addressable   being   studied;   the 
40:1219:105379:20:21:90:524:647:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:overturning  of  conventional  wisdom  through  higher-quality  research  designs  made 
40:1220:105467:21:21:90:525:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:possible by better data; and more data-driven policymaking in education. All of these are 
40:1221:105557:21:21:90:525:605:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:victories  for  both  research  and  policy. Given  the  remarkable  progress  of  computing 
40:1222:105650:21:20:90:525:584:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:power and capacity, it is in the best interest of both science and policy to make good use 
40:1223:105741:20:21:90:525:564:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:of  these  administratively-collected  data  while  following  best  practices  in  data  security 
40:1224:105840:21:21:90:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and ethics. Furthering partnerships and trust relationships between the entities that collect 
40:1225:105934:21:20:90:525:522:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:and  administer  these  administrative  data  and  members  of  the  scholarly  community,  and 
40:1226:106030:20:21:90:524:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:developing  de-identified data  sets  that  will  protect  privacy  and  confidentiality  while 
40:1227:106126:21:21:90:459:481:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:B:furthering research will benefit taxpayers, policy makers and scholars alike.  
40:1228:106202:21:21:90:93:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:!:
